Current Affairs Commentary

Hidden Worries Regarding the People's Food Problem 12

— Liu

The people's food problem does not seem to attract as much public attention today as it did before the new year. After the severe drought of the previous year, 12,960,000 metric tons of foreign rice were still imported. So far, the price of rice has been stable without major fluctuations. The general public considers this to be fortunate for the people's food supply, but it is actually not something to rejoice about. The price of rice, whether high or low, should be weighed in terms of production and consumption, considering the pros and cons. Low grain prices hurt farmers, while high grain prices hurt the people. Neither is a blessing for people's livelihood. Last year's autumn harvest varied from abundance to scarcity in Zhejiang Province. Jiangsu Province did not see a fully abundant harvest either. Anhui Province was worried about the lack of regulatory measures, and the Shanghai rice market was in a state of prolonged sluggishness and short-term surges. The price of new rice is closely related to the livelihood of farmers throughout the year. The current stagnant rice price is more of a reflection of rural bankruptcy than a result of abundant rice harvests. Since the decline of the countryside, farmers have lost their ability to save. As soon as new grain comes on the market, they urgently seek to exchange it for living expenses, not caring about future shortages. Landlords parasitic on farmers share the same fate as the farmers. Therefore, when new agricultural products come onto the market, there is often an oversupply. No one can come forward to take charge of regulation. The current rice price is supported by purchases from Yantai and Qingdao merchants. However, the sales routes for rice in the north have always been very limited. The current continuous purchases of thousands of bags are quite surprising. Yesterday's telegraph news in this newspaper stated that the puppet military and administrative ministry has controlled food supplies, wheat flour, and has ordered no exports to maintain the food and military needs within the puppet area. Yantai and Dalian are only separated by a narrow strip of water that a sail can reach. Could this be the leak?

The need for food storage and regulation is something that the Chinese people know and speak of with great emphasis. However, as time passes, they easily forget it. Occasionally, when efforts are made, they rarely succeed. A one-day burst of sunshine followed by ten days of cold will not achieve anything. In the past, the ever-normal granary was used to supply the military, and community granaries were used to prepare for famine. Later generations slightly changed the system, but opening granaries and distributing grain still benefited the people's food supply. However, the system of storing grain exists in name only. The promotion of agricultural granaries has not yet been fully beneficial. Without resources for storage, there is no preparation for disasters. This leads to low grain prices when new grain comes onto the market and no food for the people when there is a shortage. This is the situation in normal times. What will happen in times of crisis? In ancient times, there was a warning that a nation without a three-year reserve would not be a nation. Where is the three-month supply of grain now? We sit idly by as good rice flows out without thinking of remedies. When a rice shortage strikes, we will again seek help from foreign countries. Leaving aside the unbearable dangers to people's livelihood and the national economy, the losses from buying high and selling low cannot be calculated.

Main Tax Revenue Statistics for the 24th Year 14

Nanjing: The National Tax Administration of the Ministry of Finance manages the national consolidated tax, stamp tax, tobacco and alcohol tax, property tax, and customs and salt tax, which are the main sources of revenue for the national treasury. The various taxes collected by the administration in the 24th year have been classified and assessed, and preliminary statistics have been compiled. Excerpts of the figures are as follows. The total annual revenue was 136,381,000 yuan, an increase of 4,330,000 yuan compared to the 23rd year. This year, the flood-affected area was extremely large, and the market in various places was very depressed. Business closures were frequent. The administration's collection performance was still able to increase by more than 4.3 million yuan. Among them, the consolidated tax portion included 75,814,000 yuan in cigarette tax, 19,308,000 yuan in cotton yarn tax, 5,552,000 yuan in wheat flour tax, 8,805,000 yuan in match tax, 2,785,000 yuan in cement tax, 3,568,000 yuan in flue-cured tobacco tax, and 677,000 yuan in alcohol tax, totaling 116,509,000 yuan. The consolidated tax revenue in the 23rd year was 110,746,000 yuan. This year's increase was 5,763,000 yuan. The successive opening of consolidated tax in Sichuan, Gansu, and Ningxia provinces in July and August of this year was also a reason for part of the increase. The stamp tax revenue was 7,715,000 yuan (excluding the number of stamps sold by the post office in Guangdong Province). The revenue in the 23rd year was 7,490,000 yuan, an increase of 225,000 yuan. This year, there were also cases of exchanging old stamps for new stamps, which affected tax revenue. Therefore, the actual increase was more than this. In the future, this tax is expected to improve daily. The tobacco and alcohol tax (in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Henan, Hubei, Fujian, Shandong, Hebei, Chahar, and other provinces) totaled 9,672,000 yuan. The revenue in the 23rd year was 11,055,000 yuan. Due to natural disasters and banditry, there was a shortfall of 1,383,000 yuan this year. The mineral tax totaled 2,485,000 yuan. The revenue in the 23rd year was 2,760,000 yuan. For the same reasons, there was a shortfall of 275,000 yuan this year. The tax surplus and deficit statistics still show an increase as above. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Remains of Martyr Fan Hongxian Were Buried Yesterday: Representatives Were Sent by the Central Executive and Supervisory Committees to Pay Respects 16

Nanjing: The remains of Martyr Fan Hongxian were buried in the cemetery area of Maqun Bo, near the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum, on the morning of the 19th in the midst of a bleak wind and bitter rain. At 9:00 am, the procession started from the First Park. Members of the Central Committee Yu Youren, Wang Luyi, Bai Wenwei, and Zhou Bomin, as well as representatives from various agencies and organizations, totaling several hundred people, all went to hold the ropes. The procession stretched for about a mile. It was headed by a military band and a cavalry unit of the military police, followed by two companies of the Training Corps, a police security team, and the entire student body of the Beijing Anhui Middle School. The pallbearers proceeded from Baixia Road, Taiping Road, and Huangpu Road to Zhongshan Gate, arriving at the cemetery at about 11:00 am. The various committee members and representatives also waited there. At 12:00 pm, the remains were moved into the tomb, and the burial ceremony was held at 12:30 pm. The Central Executive Committee sent Yu Youren as its representative to pay respects, and the Central Supervisory Committee sent Zhang Ji as its representative. Mournful music was played, flowers were offered, and the memorial address of the Central Executive and Supervisory Committees was read. The entire assembly bowed three times to the remains of Fan, and then the ceremony ended and they dispersed. The architecture of Martyr Fan's tomb is simple and solemn, consisting of three parts: the spirit tomb, the memorial hall, and the tomb path stele pavilion, all of which have been completed. However, the tomb was only filled with earth and the construction completed after the burial. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Revolution in Paraguay: President Has Resigned: The Revolution Erupted Due to the Peace Treaty with Bolivia 18

Asuncion, Paraguay: Leaders of the Paraguayan Revolutionary Party announced today that President Ayala has resigned and General Estigarribia has also been arrested. Elections will be held soon. (18th National Telegram)

Asuncion, Paraguay: A revolution suddenly broke out in the capital yesterday. President Ayala took refuge on a warship and has now submitted his resignation to the captain for delivery. He then quietly disembarked and was not humiliated by the revolutionaries. Colonel Franco, the leader of the revolutionary movement, has returned to the country from Argentina but has not yet arrived here. It is reported that after the success of the revolutionary movement, the peace treaty with Bolivia will not be changed. (18th Havas Telegram)

Asuncion, Paraguay: Dr. Ayala, President of Paraguay, who took office on August 15, 1932, has resigned today after escaping from the capital due to a rebellion. Ayala initially fled to the Nagaya Naval Arsenal, where he resisted the rebels with the help of the military police for some time. Later, due to the overwhelming force, he took refuge on a gunboat. This afternoon, at the request of the rebel leaders, he resigned from the presidency, left the gunboat, and safely returned to his hometown. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Asuncion, Paraguay: A revolution suddenly broke out in the capital yesterday, and President Ayala resigned and left, as reported in another telegram. After the president's resignation, the revolutionary movement can be ended, and the leaders may organize a temporary military government with Senator Arocha as chairman. Colonel Franco, the leader of the revolutionary movement, has taken a plane from the capital of Argentina and is expected to arrive here at noon today. According to Colonel Gong Chiyalle, one of the leaders of the revolutionary movement, this revolution was instigated by soldiers who participated in the Chaco War. Most of them are young military officers who are dissatisfied with the government's lack of relief efforts in the economic panic. Colonel Franco, a Paraguayan national hero, was also exiled abroad, causing great indignation, which eventually led to the uprising. (18th Havas Telegram)

Buenos Aires, Argentina: Colonel Franco, the Paraguayan hero of the Chaco War, announced today that the Paraguayan revolutionary movement will abide by the Chaco War peace treaty signed by the old government. (18th National Telegram)

Asuncion, Paraguay: Soldiers who participated in the Chaco War rebelled yesterday to oppose the peace treaty signed by the government with Bolivia and claimed that the revolutionary army had controlled the entire country. The government expressed its surrender at 10 pm last night. President Ayala is now taking refuge on a warship in the Paraguay River. Foreign Minister Riato is being held at the Army Aviation School. Colonel Smith led the revolutionaries last night to welcome Colonel Franco to the capital. Franco, a hero of the Chaco War, went into exile in Argentina on February 3 due to the exposure of his revolutionary plan. This revolution was sparked by the peace treaty signed between Paraguay and Bolivia and the government's approval last Saturday of US President Roosevelt's call for a Pan-American peace conference. President Ayala and the government forces led by General Estigarribia, the former commander-in-chief of the Paraguayan army in the Chaco, engaged in fierce fighting with the revolutionary army at 7 am yesterday. (18th National Telegram)

Japanese Foreign Ministry and Army Decide to Resolve Issues with Russia Peacefully: Will Demand that Soviet Russia Extradite Rebel Soldiers 21

Tokyo: According to semi-official sources here, Japan will demand that Soviet Russia immediately extradite the rebel soldiers of "Manchukuo" who rebelled in Mishan on January 29 and fled into Russian territory after fighting with the Japanese-Manchu forces at Jinjiagou. Since the repeated border clashes and the tense situation, senior officials of the Japanese Army Ministry and the Foreign Ministry have been holding meetings almost every day. It is heard that the two ministries have decided to seek peaceful solutions to the border incidents. Tokyo: Director Murakami of the Military Affairs Section of the Ministry of the Army visited Director-General Togo of the Eurasian Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 5 pm on the 19th to discuss various agreements regarding the Manchuria-Soviet Union and Manchuria-Mongolia border issues. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Army shared the same opinion on this matter. Therefore, Foreign Minister Hirota will soon issue instructions to Ambassador Ota stationed in the Soviet Union regarding the rejection of the participation of a third country. (19th Allied News Agency Telegram)

Japan, Manchukuo, and Russia should quickly establish an investigation committee to determine the border line. The Soviet government, in the past China-Russia Treaty and Russia-Fengtian Treaty, expressed its agreement to determine the border line in the area. It deliberately expressed its agreement to Japan's proposal and removed the root of border disputes. However, the Director-General of the Soviet Foreign Ministry replied to this proposal that there was no place where the border was unclear and that the border crossing incident was unrelated to the border line and was caused by Japan's and Manchukuo's active policies. Japanese Fighter Planes Collide: One Person Falls into the Sea and is Missing 25

Saiki: At 8:50 am on the 19th, two ship-based attack aircraft of the Saiki Naval Air Corps collided during high-altitude combat training, and both fell into the sea at the same time, disappearing from sight. Of the six airmen, only Petty Officer Kanazawa was rescued. The other five are missing. The air corps immediately dispatched aircraft to search, and patrol boats were also dispatched to assist in the search, but it seems that all have been killed in action. The missing personnel are as follows: Airman Second Class Akai Toshiyo, Airman Second Class Hata Shigezo, Petty Officer Inoue Masanosuke, and Petty Officer Nagasaki Matsutaro (19th Allied Telegram)

Kochi: At 9:30 am on the 19th, an aircraft carried by the battleship Yamashiro, which was staying in Sukumo Port in Kochi Prefecture, caught fire while training on the sea surface of Sukumo Bay, flying at an altitude of 200 meters. A passing ship, the No. 2 Sukumo Maru, discovered the incident. A lieutenant and an airman on board jumped into the sea and were immediately rescued. Both suffered burns to their faces and other areas but were not life-threatening. The aircraft was towed to Sukumo Bay by the ship. (19th Allied Telegram)

Focus of Japanese Election: Controlled Currency vs. Currency Inflation 26

The main issue in this election that the people should support is the policy of controlled currency inflation advocated by Finance Minister Takahashi or the policy of unrestricted currency inflation advocated by the Seiyukai. After a Victory in the East African War, Anxiously Seeking to Reverse the Declining Trend in Central Europe; Hoping to Draw Closer to Germany by Replicating the Old Tactic of Countering Russia, Aiming to Maintain Influence in the Danube River Region and Preserve Austria's Independence 27

Rome, special dispatch from our correspondent: The Italian authorities intend to take advantage of their military victory against the Abyssinians to consolidate their diplomatic front. The Deputy Foreign Minister, Suvich, after meeting with the German Ambassador to Italy, Hassel, yesterday, is scheduled to meet with the Austrian Foreign Minister, Weidegger, in Florence today to discuss various pending issues, particularly the Danube River Pact. It is reported that Suvich will explain to Weidegger that if the Danube River issue is resolved under Soviet guidance, the danger would be significant. As for the rapprochement between Italy and Germany, it will not hinder Austrian independence in any way, as Italy has no intention of abandoning its stance on guaranteeing Austrian independence. Its rapprochement with Germany is based on the promise provided by the German leader, Hitler, regarding Austrian independence. Suvich will also express that although Italy is currently engaged in East Africa, its strength in Europe remains strong, and its commitment to the Stresa Front and the Locarno Treaty will depend on the attitude of Britain and France towards Italy, thus giving Italy more flexibility in dealing with Britain and France. In short, the rapprochement between Italy and Germany is intended to establish a better understanding without affecting future relations with Britain and France. The reason for not wanting to make demands on the redistribution of mandated territories is to show respect for the existing interests of Britain and France. Furthermore, the movement towards rapprochement between Italy and Germany began as early as September of last year, when Italian newspapers expressed their approval of German policies, especially Germany's views on the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact, the Locarno Pact, and Germany's rearmament. German newspapers also expressed sympathy for Italy's military action in Abyssinia. The two sides were already very harmonious in sentiment. In addition, Italy is determined to maintain its original influence in the Danube River region and opposes the Soviet Union's control of the Danube River region. This, along with Germany's rejection of the Soviet Union, is actually converging on the same path. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Rome: Since the outbreak of the war, special expenditures from various departments have been urgently needed. The Ministry of Finance has recently decided to increase the funding for the following departments: 40 million lire for the Colonial Department, 500 million lire for the Army Department, 200 million lire for the Navy Department, 350 million lire for the Air Force Department, and 80 million lire for the Ministry of Interior. The last item is specifically for supporting the families of soldiers on expeditions. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Rome: The German Ambassador to Italy, Hassel, was summoned back to his country in the middle of last week to meet with the German leader, Hitler, in Munich, and then immediately returned to his post. British Company Releases Last Year's Silver Market Annual Report; Three Major Changes in Finance 30

London: The British company, Montagu & Co., today released its annual report on the silver market, stating that there were three major changes in the financial sector in 1935: the instability of the United States' silver policy, Mexico's abandonment of the silver standard, and China's de facto abandonment of silver. Although the United States purchased a total of 544,000,000 ounces of silver last year, its silver reserves are still far from the 1:3 ratio of silver to gold, because the United States' gold reserves have greatly increased. The world's new silver mine output in 1935 was a total of 206,000,000 ounces, an increase of 21,000,000 ounces compared to the output in 1934, and the supply of silver from other sources in 1935 was 145,000,000 ounces. The main factor in the silver market in the future will of course still be the US Treasury Department. The policies that the US Treasury Department will implement have not yet been indicated. US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau recently stated that the US monetary policy is based on a 24-hour foundation, which makes it difficult to grasp. India has recently shown signs of increasing its silver purchases. The restoration of the silver standard in China is unlikely for the time being, and China will continue to sell silver as a way to maintain currency exchange rates. Therefore, the silver market can only rely on one buyer. If this buyer suddenly changes its policy, it will inevitably have a disruptive impact on banks and will require some time to adjust to the new situation. Therefore, as long as the US Treasury Department's measures are not clear, the future of the silver market remains uncertain, and it is practically impossible to predict the future trend of silver prices. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Soviet Deputy Defense Minister Leaves France 31

Spanish Military Plots Coup; Current Cabinet Announces Resignation; Police and Left-Wing Parties Mobilize; Right-Wing Conspires for Dictatorship 33

Madrid: Valladares, the leader of the Liberal Party, who took office on December 30, has resigned as Prime Minister today. Azaña, the former Prime Minister and Army Minister, has reportedly agreed to form a new cabinet. Azaña, 56, is the leader of the United Republican Party. When he served as Prime Minister between 1932 and 1933, he granted women the right to vote. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Madrid: The cabinet held a State Council meeting at the Presidential Palace at 1:35 PM today, and then announced its collective resignation at 2:30 PM. Beforehand, Prime Minister Valladares made a statement to reporters, saying, "The cabinet members respect the spirit of democracy and the will of the people, and have decided to step aside." (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Madrid: Barrio, the leader of the Republican Union, stated today that the government has decided to resign, and Azaña may succeed in forming a moderate left-wing cabinet. It is said that before the general election, the left-wing parties and the Republican factions reached an agreement that no matter how the left-wing wins, the power will still be controlled by the Republican factions. Therefore, although the Socialist Party, Communist Party, and Syndicalist Party occupy a majority in the Congress, they may not be included in the new cabinet. At the same time, military leaders are also holding secret meetings. (National News dispatch, 19th)

Madrid: The situation deteriorated last night, and some military leaders planned to seize power, but an army colonel, unwilling to participate in the coup, informed the authorities. The authorities immediately dispatched the militia and took preemptive action before the plot could unfold, arresting two senior military officers. One of them is reportedly General Goded, the Army Inspector General. The London Daily News' Madrid dispatch stated that the purpose of this coup was to restore the monarchy through a dictatorship. If the plot succeeds, the deposed King Alfonso, who was forced to abdicate in 1931, will soon return to Spain. To establish a dictatorship, fascist and royalist officers in the army have formed a secret organization called the Spanish Military Union. Inspections are now very strict, and newspapers are not allowed to publish news of the coup. The general public is still unaware of this matter. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Madrid: Today, the police, the Socialist Party, and the Communist Party are all engaged in general mobilization. The public is paying close attention to this, fearing that disturbances may occur at any time. After the Police Commissioner hurriedly returned to the capital from Zaragoza, he immediately summoned all police chiefs to headquarters and ordered them to implement general mobilization. At the same time, the headquarters of the "Left-Wing People's Front Party," the Socialist Party, and the Communist Party are also implementing general mobilization, and many party members are carrying weapons. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Spain; Election Results Revealed; Left-Wing Parties Win a Landslide Victory 34

Madrid: According to unofficial statistics, the approximate number of seats won by each party in the renewed House of Representatives election is as follows: Right-Wing Parties won a total of 144 seats, including 102 seats for the People's Action Party led by the former Army Minister Gil Robles, 23 seats for the Royalist Party, 12 seats for the Right-Wing Independent faction, and 7 seats for the Catalan Autonomous Right-Wing faction. Central Parties won a total of 45 seats, including 14 seats for the government's Central Party, 4 seats for the Conservative Republican Party, 4 seats for the Progressive Party, 13 seats for the Agrarian Party, 8 seats for the Radical Party, and 2 seats for the Liberal Democratic Party. Left-Wing Parties won a total of 233 seats, including 81 seats for the Socialist Party, 75 seats for the Left-Wing Republican Party, 33 seats for the Unified Republican Party, 30 seats for the Catalan Autonomous Left-Wing faction, 11 seats for the Communist Party, 2 seats for the Federalist Party, and 1 seat for the Syndicalist faction. Basque Nationalists won 5 seats, and others won 5 seats. The total number of seats is 432. According to this, the full results of the election have not yet been announced, and second-round voting is required in some constituencies. However, the general public is confident that the left-wing parties will win a majority. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

League of Nations to Meet Next Month; Discussing Oil Embargo Against Italy; Britain and France Have No Preparation for New Peace Talks 35

London: The League of Nations Assembly's Committee of Eighteen will meet in Geneva next month to discuss the issue of an oil embargo against Italy. The British government has appointed Foreign Secretary Eden to attend the committee. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Geneva: Regarding the date of the meeting of the League of Nations Assembly's Committee of Eighteen, according to our correspondent, the chairman of the committee, the Portuguese representative Vasconcelos, and the French Foreign Minister Flandin, both advocate convening on March 9. The British Foreign Office advocates convening on March 2. League of Nations officials also agree with March 9 for two reasons: the League of Nations' new building has been completed, but the interior has not yet been fully furnished; and there are other committees that are scheduled to meet on March 2, creating a conflict in time. As for the oil sanctions, League of Nations officials believe that even if the United States cannot participate, they must be implemented for three reasons: First, the results of the expert committee's research on the oil embargo are sufficient to prove that after the League of Nations member states implement the oil embargo, Italy will find it more difficult to obtain supplies and its expenditures will increase. Second, after the member states implement financial sanctions against Italy, even if Italy purchases oil from non-member states, its burden will inevitably increase. Third, if the representatives of the countries belonging to the Committee of Eighteen have unanimous opinions and firm attitudes, it is expected that the United States will not completely stand aside. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

London: Foreign Secretary Lord Stanhope, in response to Lord Phillimore's question during a debate on foreign policy in the Upper House today, stated that he has taken steps to promote a peaceful resolution to the Italo-Abyssinian War, saying that he has not yet received any requests from the Italian or Abyssinian sides to consider peace talks. The British government and other League of Nations member states are not prepared to put forward new proposals for reconciliation. Today, Lord Buxton first spoke, supporting actions to promote a peaceful resolution, saying that this could consolidate the collective peace system and end Abyssinia's slavery and slave trade with international assistance. Next, Lord Cecil spoke, urging the government to pursue a resolute and unified policy. Lords Lloyd, Mansfield, and Mottistone then spoke in succession, criticizing the League of Nations' policy of imposing sanctions on Italy for resorting to force. Lord Ponsonby supported the previous three with his peace proposals, but Lord Strabolgi and other Labor peers expressed dissent to Ponsonby's views. Lord Davies spoke, saying that if the government's policy is accepted by public opinion supporting the League of Nations, then it should focus on seeking a peaceful resolution to the dispute in accordance with the principles of the League of Nations Covenant. After the speeches, Foreign Secretary Lord Stanhope gave the above-mentioned response on behalf of the government, saying that making peace proposals to Italy now would only encourage Italy to hope for better terms. If proposals that encourage Italy to continue the war are put forward, it will not be conducive to peace. At one point, sanctions against Italy did agitate the Italians, almost unanimously supporting Mussolini, but today the situation is different. Increasing the pressure of sanctions is now having an effect. Although sanctions have shown the world that a war of aggression is not worth the cost, it is not yet possible to say that this has been achieved, but he is very optimistic and believes that the League of Nations will demonstrate its ability to succeed. Currently, all League of Nations member states, except for three, have persisted in implementing the sanctions. The British government does not want to take unilateral action on this dispute. As for an oil embargo against Italy, the British government does not want to express any opinion before the League of Nations fully discusses the matter. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

US Neutrality Act Extension; Senate Also Passes; Now Awaiting President Roosevelt's Signature 36

Washington: The Senate today passed the bill to extend the validity of the current Neutrality Act to May 1, 1937. This bill has been passed by the House of Representatives and has now been sent to the White House for President Roosevelt's signature. The two points of the current Neutrality Act that have been amended are as follows: a complete ban on belligerent countries borrowing from the United States; and countries in the Americas are not bound by the Act. (National News dispatch, 18th)

Washington: The Senate today passed an amendment to the bill to extend the US Neutrality Act to May 1, 1927, advocating that the export of military equipment should not exceed peacetime levels, but there was a great outcry against it in the whole house, so this amendment was not even put to a vote and was dropped. Someone also moved to amend it to allow the president to have the right to deny government protection to American ships in war zones and to hold American citizens responsible for trading with belligerent countries, but these were all rejected by the Senate. It has been learned that this Neutrality Act was previously passed by the House of Representatives. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

New York: US Secretary of War Dern, in a speech at a dinner party at the New York Happy Association tonight, said that a Neutrality Act alone is not enough to prevent war. The Neutrality Act seems to contain elements of selfish isolationism. A policy of protecting one's own skin and flesh, regardless of the unconscionable and depraved behavior of some rogue states, does not seem to be something that people who believe in freedom and justice should adopt. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Battleship Tonnage Issue; France's Attitude Determined; Accepting 35,000 Tons; But With a Five-Year Limit 37

London: The French Chief Delegate to the Naval Conference, Ambassador Corbin, returned to his country a few days ago to report to the government on the situation at the Naval Conference. Yesterday, the French Minister of the Navy, Pietri, convened a meeting to discuss the matter. According to reports in Parisian newspapers, France may ultimately accept 35,000 tons as the tonnage of battleships, but only for a period of five years, after which it must be reduced. (Note: Britain originally advocated that future treaties should stipulate general qualitative restrictions and a system for exchanging shipbuilding information, and that their validity should be ten years.) The British side does not object to this view. What is unknown is what the US attitude will be. Naval circles here believe that the work of the Naval Conference cannot be seriously progressed until the United States has given its reply. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Washington: The French Ambassador to the United States, de Laboulaye, and the Undersecretary of State, Phillips, met at the State Department yesterday afternoon to discuss the tonnage of battleships at the Naval Conference and the invitation to Germany to participate in future agreements. Afterwards, de Laboulaye was unwilling to comment on the details of the talks. However, according to our correspondent, the United States insists on its original position that battleships should be limited to 35,000 tons. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

London: The Naval Conference has now entered its final stage. An American lawyer has arrived to assist in drafting the treaty. The instructions sent by France today have clarified the situation, as the issue of battleship tonnage, which was previously an obstacle to a comprehensive compromise, has now reportedly been shelved by these instructions. The French Ambassador to Britain is currently making a final effort to persuade the United States to reduce its 35,000-ton figure, but if the US government insists on not agreeing, France will abandon its claim that battleships should be limited to 37,000 tons. The next two weeks will be devoted to the work of sorting out the wording of the treaty, and then the four countries of Britain, France, Italy, and the United States will nod their heads and recognize it as a kind of pre-determined book, but it will not come into effect until Japan, Germany, and Russia have signed it. Russia will be invited to sign this autumn, but will not be invited to participate in the conference. France is very willing to have a separate agreement restricting air forces outside the naval treaty, and the establishment of a mutual assistance pact in the skies between the Locarno countries to supplement it. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

French Female Reporter Predicts a Major War Next Summer: Japan to Attack Soviet Russia and Germany to Invade Holland 40

Paris – Mrs. Tai Puyi Xu, a political reporter for the "Wodair" newspaper in Paris, published an article today predicting that a world war will break out in Europe in the summer of 1937, or possibly even earlier. She believes that the countries involved at the outbreak of war will include Germany, France, Japan, Soviet Russia, Holland, Belgium, Czechoslovakia, and Romania, and that other countries will certainly join later. Mrs. Xu further states that, according to military strategists, Germany will launch a surprise attack on Holland and Romania. At the same time, Japan in the Far East will launch an offensive against Soviet Russia in support. The German troops attacking Holland can be divided into three main forces. The first force will cross the Maas River and advance towards Calais. The second force, taking advantage of Holland's incomplete mobilization, will use swift and decisive means to destroy all its defensive actions. The third force will cross the Dutch border with armored vehicles and tanks, aiming for the Zuiderzee to cut off communication between the north and south of Holland and isolate its northern region. Therefore, the German army can occupy the entire territory of Holland in just a few hours. From there, they can then attack Belgium, seize the ports on the North Sea, and use submarines to cut off communication between England and France. As for the Eastern Front, Poland may join forces with Germany to pass through Czechoslovakia in ten days and cross Romania to attack the Ukraine of Soviet Russia. (Fifteenth National Telegram)

Regulations for Commercial Attachés at Foreign Embassies 48

Nanjing – The Executive Yuan has approved the eight articles of the regulations for commercial attachés at foreign embassies. The contents are as follows: 1. Commercial attachés shall be established at foreign embassies and important commercial ports. 2. Commercial attachés shall be divided into two categories: commercial attachés and commercial commissioners. Commercial attachés shall be appointed through simplified or recommended procedures, and commercial commissioners shall be appointed through recommended procedures. 3. The duties of commercial attachés shall include: investigating and reporting on the financial, transportation, taxation, and general industrial conditions of the host country; promoting and publicizing domestic products; handling matters entrusted by the government; and handling investigation matters entrusted by the International Trade Bureau and domestic public and private industrial organizations. 4. Commercial attachés shall be under the direction and supervision of the Chinese ambassador or minister in the host country. 5. Commercial attachés may establish Chinese and foreign language secretariats or clerks when necessary. (Nineteenth Special Telegram)

Ministry of Railways Releases Statistics on Railway Accidents 49

Nanjing – According to the Ministry of Railways' statistics, from January 1934 to June 1935, a total of 6,787 railway accidents occurred on railways across the country in 18 months. The most common causes were engine damage and bearing burnout. Derailments and fatalities also accounted for a portion of the accidents. On the 19th, the Ministry of Railways specifically listed the causes of the various accidents and issued a notice ordering all railways to conduct regular inspections in order to reduce accidents in the future. It also stated that the increase or decrease in accidents on each railway will be used as a measure of their operational performance. (Nineteenth Special Telegram)

Statistics on Divorce Cases in One Year 50

Nanjing – According to statistics from the Ministry of Judicial Administration, among divorce cases from July 1933 to June 1934, Jiangsu Province had the most with 90 cases, followed by Zhejiang Province with 69 cases. In general, the more developed and open-minded a city is, the more divorce cases there are. Among those who divorced, women under the age of 20 were more than twice as likely to divorce as men, while men over the age of 30 were more than twice as likely to divorce as women. This is because older men have economic means and are not worried about not being able to remarry, while older women face difficulties in remarrying due to their age and declining appearance. The reasons for divorce include: bigamy (39 cases), adultery (48 cases), abuse by the other party (132 cases), abuse by relatives (58 cases), abandonment (69 cases), attempted murder (8 cases), serious illness (23 cases), mental illness (15 cases), unknown whereabouts (24 cases), and criminal offenses (31 cases). Of these, men filed for divorce in 104 cases, and women filed for divorce in 344 cases. (Nineteenth Central News Agency Telegram)

Ministry of Railways Revises Regulations for Calculating Pig Transportation Fees 51

Nanjing – The Ministry of Railways has revised the regulations for calculating railway transportation fees for pigs and ordered all railways to implement them starting next month, the first day. 1. Pigs weighing less than 10 kilograms each are considered piglets and will be charged according to the fourth class and actual weight. Pigs weighing 20 kilograms or more are considered adult pigs and will be charged per head at a rate of 5 jiao per kilometer. (Nineteenth Central News Agency Telegram)

Salt Merchants: Methods for Lending Money Against Huai Salt 52

Nanjing – The Inspectorate General previously submitted a report to the Ministry of Finance stating that due to the overproduction of salt in the Huainan region, salt merchants purchasing excess salt quantities do not have sufficient capital to circulate and need to apply for loans from banks. The government may provide appropriate assistance, but the scope of assistance is limited to guaranteeing that when the salt pledged as collateral by the bank is sold, the government will deduct a certain amount from the salt price to repay the creditor until the principal and interest of the loan are fully repaid. Before the deduction is made, the salt will not be released. If the loan is not repaid when the new salt law is implemented and the salt pledged as collateral has not yet been sold, the government can guarantee the opportunity to sell it off. The Ministry of Finance reviewed the report and found that the proposed methods were appropriate and approved them. Nineteenth Central News Agency Telegram

Judicial Yuan Clarifies the Definition of Gambling Crimes 60

Nanjing – The Ministry of Interior sent a letter to the Judicial Yuan requesting clarification on the definition of gambling crimes. The Judicial Yuan explained that the crime defined in Article 266, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code requires that the act be committed in a public place or a place accessible to the public. The act defined in Article 45, Paragraph 1 of the Law on Punishment of Violations of Public Order also requires that the act be committed on a road or in a public place. Therefore, gambling in a residence or shop, even if the gamblers and gambling tools are easily visible from the outside or the gambling sounds are easily heard from the outside, does not conform to the aforementioned legal provisions. However, if it falls under the circumstances of Article 267 or Article 268 of the Criminal Code, it should be punished separately according to those articles. A letter has been sent to the Ministry of Interior for verification. (Nineteenth Special Telegram)

Ningxia Provincial Government and Alxa Banner's Dispute Over the Dengkou County Seat: Both Sides Have Telegraphed the Central Government to State Their Reasons; Tang Kesan's Mediation and Resolution Are Still Pending 76

Beiping Correspondence: Since the dispute arose regarding Alxa Banner's request to abolish the Dengkou County seat in Ningxia, rumors have been rampant, and opinions have been divided. Tang Kesan, a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, was dispatched north to Alxa Banner via Beiping to mediate. He has now returned to Ningxia and met with Ma Hongkui, the chairman of the provincial government. However, because the six conditions proposed by Alxa Banner far exceed the scope of ordinary negotiations, a resolution is still pending. Fearing that distant rumors might distort the truth, Ma Hongkui specifically sent a letter to Bai Jianmin, the resident representative in Beiping, explaining the details of the dispute for clarification. The complete documents are recorded below:

Alxa Banner Proposes Six Conditions

As a result of the mediation by Tang Kesan, a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, in Alxa Banner, the banner proposed six conditions at Sakeda Lizhara to seek a resolution. The content includes: The sovereignty of Dengkou still belongs to this banner; the Dengkou County government will not be abolished temporarily but will report to the central government in the shortest possible time to withdraw from the banner's territory; the land temporarily occupied by the Dengkou County government should be given a corresponding rent (rent for the county government's land was paid in previous years); the area from Dengkou south to Shizuishan (about 120 li) will be temporarily administered by the Dengkou County government on behalf of the banner, and it should be returned to the banner as soon as the Dengkou County government withdraws from the banner; all administrative powers in places such as Wulan Mutu, Fujiawanzi, Shang Jiang Ershiliuzi, Sanshenggong, Guangqingyuan, and Dukoutang above Dengkou should not be interfered with by the Dengkou County government of the province, and the names of the county government office and various district offices in Guangqingyuan should be abolished immediately; the tax bureaus and checkpoints set up by the provincial government in places such as Dengkou Tukemudu, Dashuigou, and Daobulu within the banner should be returned to the banner immediately to handle them independently in accordance with regulations; unless there are special circumstances, mutual assistance should be provided, and after prior consultation and agreement, the provincial government should not arbitrarily send troops to garrison in any place within the banner.

Ma Hongkui's Telegram to Jiang and Huang

Ma Hongkui sent a telegram to Jiang Jieshi, the President of the Executive Yuan, and Huang Musong, the Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, stating: "Urgent telegram. Member Tang Kesan returned to Ningxia from Alxa Banner and stated in person that he was ordered to mediate the Dengkou County establishment case. After repeated persuasion, the banner finally did not insist on abolishing the county seat but proposed six requirements, which are quite astonishing to read. Member Tang must have submitted a separate report detailing the situation, hoping to have it noted. The establishment of Dengkou County was due to the increasing number of foreigners renting land and reclaiming land in the area north of Dengkou after the Boxer Rebellion in the Gengzi year of the previous Qing dynasty, as well as the free land reclamation by the people of this province. Over the years, it has developed into a densely populated area. At that time, the farmers in that area were all Han Chinese who migrated from Pingluo County in Ningxia. All civil and criminal lawsuits had to be filed with the Pingluo County government. The roads were long and remote, causing great inconvenience. In addition, that area has always been the key to the northern gate of Ningxia, holding the central hub of Bao Ning's transportation. Various tax bureaus, salt bureaus, and telegraph bureaus all require effective protection by the government. Therefore, the Gansu Provincial Government, before the establishment of Ningxia Province in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, based on the facts and local needs, requested the central government to approve the establishment of a county for separate administration. For six or seven years, peace has prevailed, and Alxa Banner has never raised any objections. Since I took office, considering the special circumstances of the county, most of the land has been leased to churches for reclamation and operation due to the Boxer Indemnity. Before the provincial government has raised funds to redeem it, everything has been maintained as it is, and there are no other facilities. Guangqingyuan and its surrounding areas have always been the garrison of Gansu troops, but the barracks were destroyed by Sun's army, and not a single soldier has been stationed there since. Local security is purely the responsibility of the county. Last year, the Red bandits fled westward, and Mao and Liu joined forces in northern Shaanxi, approaching Ningbian Dengkou, making defense extremely urgent. Comprehensively considering the situation, I reluctantly ordered the county to train militiamen to strengthen their self-defense capabilities. Alxa Banner repeatedly obstructed it, and after explanation, there were no other expressions. Now, after reading the six requirements of the banner, they completely obliterate the facts and overturn the established case. Not only can the central government's decrees be blatantly disregarded, but even if the provincial government abandons its duty to defend the territory, how can the Han Chinese in the county willingly accept it? Where will their insatiable demands end? For example, the third requirement states that the area from Dengkou south to Shizuishan will be temporarily administered by the Dengkou County government on behalf of the banner, and it should be returned to the banner as soon as the Dengkou County government withdraws from the banner. Nothing is more absurd and ridiculous than this. The distance from Dengkou to Shizuishan is 120 li, but the sandy shore along the river is only half a li wide and has always been barren. Since there are no residents, why bother with the county government's proxy administration? Moreover, Dengkou is named after the place, which must have a fixed scope and is not comparable to nomadic areas. The banner's requirement is merely an attempt to temporarily conceal its true intentions in order to achieve its goal of abolishing the county seat. However, geographical and historical relations cannot be vaguely obliterated. Comprehensively reviewing all the requirements, the fourth requirement, which states that the provincial government and Dengkou County shall not interfere with the administrative powers of Wulan Mutu, Fujiawanzi, Shang Jiang Ershiliuzi, Sanshenggong, Guangqingyuan, Dukoutang, and other places above Dengkou, is even more contrary to the facts. The division of governance in a country is based on land and people. In the past, the Gansu Provincial Government, considering that the Han Chinese who migrated from Pingluo County had been managing Wulan Mutu, Fujiawanzi, and other places under Dengkou for many years and were becoming increasingly prosperous, established the county in response to the needs of the times. If the administrative power of that area cannot be interfered with by the county government, then the Dengkou County government is truly a castle in the air. Why bother with the establishment of the county at that time? Moreover, after the establishment of the county, it was divided into districts for management. Why did Alxa Banner have no objections at that time? There is no justification for it in theory or in practice. As for the fifth requirement, the tax bureaus and checkpoints set up by the provincial government in places such as Dengkou Tukemudu, Dashuigou, and Daobulu within the banner should be returned to the banner for independent management. Regardless of whether the banner has the right to set up bureaus and collect taxes, the unified tax system in Dengkou County was established in the early years of the Republic of China and was not originally owned by the banner. Therefore, there is no question of returning this institution. Since Ningxia was changed to a province, this unified tax has been a major source of revenue for the provincial army. The establishment of branch checkpoints by the Dengkou Tax Bureau in places such as Tukemudu Dashuigou is also a decades-old established case and does not interfere with Alxa Banner. The Shuofang Dao Zhi records it in detail and can be reviewed. Moreover, successive governments in Ningxia have covered the expenses of Dengkou County from the provincial treasury and have never collected a single penny from the farmers in various districts. However, they have never dared to abandon their obligations to maintain transportation, protect the people, and build the Bao Ning Highway recently. The banner had no suggestions or recommendations for local affairs before and after the establishment of Dengkou County. Why would it want to seize the bureaus and checkpoints that have been established for decades? Who would believe that it is not taking advantage of the opportunity to coerce? Moreover, the central government has formulated regulations for the Mongolian Political Council, stipulating that counties shall not be established in Mongolian areas where counties have not been established, and that areas where counties have already been established shall continue to be handled according to the original plan. The decree is clear and cannot be ignored. Moreover, if this tax bureau can be run by the banner itself, then why can't the banner reclaim and run the existing central government agencies in the county, such as the salt tax bureau, telegraph bureau, and post office, with their insatiable demands? A little concession will surely be used as an excuse, and future responses will be extremely difficult. I am stationed in Ningxia, concerned about the current difficulties. I have heard that the banner is complaining, and I am truly afraid that the county magistrate of the county will be too hasty in responding. I have already transferred him to the province and appointed another commissioner to take over, with the sole intention of showing concession and fulfilling the central government's intention to appease the Mongolian people. I did not expect them to take an inch and demand a foot, making such excessive demands. I am fulfilling the laws and regulations and have no preconceived notions. However, I am particularly afraid that if I make too many concessions, the system will be distorted, the laws will be ineffective, and the future of the Northwest will become more complicated. As for the banner's financial difficulties, it may be true. In the future, for the sake of settling the matter and appeasing the people, the provincial government can still discuss providing assistance within its capabilities. Your Excellency travels through the nine border regions, handling countless matters every day. What I have stated is what I believe is appropriate. I respectfully request your wise decision. I am extremely anxious. Your subordinate, Ma Hongkui, bows."

Alxa Banner's Report to the Ministries and Commissions

Alxa Banner's report to the Ministry of Interior and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission states: "One report is for the urgent matter of being infringed upon, dispatching personnel to state the situation, and earnestly requesting prompt relief. Since Ningxia Province built fortresses in the Guangqingyuan area of our banner, intending to move the county seat there, our banner has previously prevented it. Recently, the Dengkou County officials have been moved to Guangqingyuan, forcibly occupying houses and implementing official duties. Furthermore, large troops have been dispatched to garrison there, intending to use force to suppress, build fortresses, and forcibly establish the county seat. We have always responded with peaceful methods. Although we have repeatedly negotiated reasonably, they have been ignored. The boundary between our banner and Ningxia Province has always been extremely clear and can be verified. Since the establishment of Dengkou County, all intrusions by Ningxia Province have been justified by the jurisdiction of Dengkou County. Therefore, the disputes in our banner are all caused by the establishment of Dengkou County. If Dengkou County is not abolished, the difficulties of our banner will not end. The establishment of Dengkou County was originally based on the report by Ningxia Province that the territory of Pingluo County was vast and difficult to govern, requesting to divide and establish it. It is clear that Dengkou County should be established within the territory of Pingluo. However, it has now been established within the territory of our banner and is constantly expanding. Recently, troops have been dispatched to press the border and forcibly occupy the area. The people of our banner are extremely indignant. We should personally go to your ministry to state everything in person and request a solution. However, due to the entanglement of banner affairs, we cannot separate. Therefore, we have specifically dispatched Chen Erde Ni Batu, the leader of the delegation, to report the actual situation. We hereby submit a document to request your ministry to review and verify the facts and earnestly request that Dengkou County be withdrawn from our banner's territory in order to quell the dispute. As for the establishment of bureaus by Ningxia Province within the inland areas of our banner to collect taxes and various other matters, we also ask for proper measures to be shown to clarify the jurisdiction of our banner and hope for a speedy resolution. We are infinitely grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Interior, Alxa Banner Zhasake Dali Zhaya."

Ningxia Provincial Government's Reply to the Ministries and Commissions

The Ningxia Provincial Government's reply to the Ministry of Interior and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission states, "Inquiry reveals that Guangqingyuan, which belongs to Dengkou County, has always been the garrison of Gansu troops. At the beginning of the establishment of the province in the eighteenth year, the Executive Yuan approved the change to a county, and the area was designated as the second administrative district of the county. Over the past seven years, great efforts have been made to cultivate the land, and everything has progressed quite well. People are engaged in commerce and agriculture, and they are all happy to comply. During the provincial political conferences held in the province two years ago, local representatives proposed redeeming the land rights. The provincial government has not yet implemented it. Unexpectedly, Alxa Banner has a very strong feudal ideology. Hearing this situation, they were sincerely afraid that the recovery would be inconvenient for them in the future, so they became covetous. Colluding with the secret church, they began by saying that they occupied their vassal territory, and then demanded the abolition of the county, trying to use this as a buffer. The provincial government did not care about it, as there is no distinction between this border and that border in the national territory. They also exhausted their reasons and subsided silently. Last autumn, the Red bandits fled westward, and the defenses of the three borders were tight. We were ordered by the central government to defend against the Red bandits, so we trained militiamen in each county and built blockhouses. I also stationed troops in the common area to consolidate the defenses. The county government established an office to facilitate administration and planned to restore the old fortresses to prepare for the stationing of troops. Unfortunately, Alxa Banner did not understand this intention and sent several teams of border officials to interfere unreasonably, exerting undue pressure, and the situation was bound to escalate. In order to settle the matter and appease the people, the provincial government sent personnel to negotiate and handle it peacefully. The matter was settled, but Alxa Banner secretly used means, slandering and attacking incessantly. Judging by their intentions, they wanted to take advantage of the national crisis to collude with various parties and conspire to abolish the county in order to achieve their private aim of encroachment. Obviously, there is another background. The interests of the provincial government are involved, and we will never rest. Therefore, we have copied the files of the previous requests to abolish the county (see the above documents) and hope that you will interact with all parties in Beiping at all times, explaining in detail, so that the truth will be revealed and the incident can be resolved. I specifically publicize this and wish you a happy spring, Ma Hongkui."

Doihara's Talk on the Hebei-Chahar Incident: Claims That Liu Guitang and Li Shouxin Have Nothing to Do With the Japanese and Puppets; Negotiations Between the Two Sides Are in Private Exchange of Opinions 77

Beiping Correspondence: In the Hebei-Chahar negotiations, the Hebei East issue is difficult to resolve, and Yin Rugeng's attitude remains unyielding. Doihara, the chief of the special service agency of the Kwantung Army stationed in Shenyang, recently went to Tongzhou to meet with Yin once. Therefore, the negotiations between the two sides are still in a private exchange of opinions, and the date of formal negotiations cannot be determined for the time being.

Doihara recently told visitors in Beiping, "I plan to stay in Beiping for another three weeks and then return to Changchun. The rumor that I (Doihara refers to himself) have been hired as a senior advisor is not true. I am only discussing North China issues with the North China authorities in a private capacity." "The work of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee has made considerable progress recently, and the administration of Hebei, Chahar, Beiping, and Tianjin has gradually become clearer." "I personally am not an 'anti-Western ideology' person and do not advocate 'Asia is for Asians' or do this work, but I am completely based on Eastern culture and strive for the peace and happiness of the Eastern people." "My actions in North China at this time have been sympathized with and understood by the authorities in North China. The Nanjing authorities may also understand in the future. In March last year, I had a long talk with former President of the Executive Yuan Wang Jingwei in Nanjing, and he expressed considerable sympathy for my actions, but I had no opportunity to meet with Chairman Jiang at that time." "Regarding the increase of troops stationed in North China, I have not yet received any official documents from my country on this matter. The number of increases is not yet known, but according to my personal speculation, it will not increase too much. The purpose of increasing troops is to protect Japanese residents, not to invade North China's land. Because the number of Japanese residents in North China is increasing, there is this need." "Outsiders often question whether North China will break away from the Nanjing central government and become completely independent. I personally cannot represent the North China authorities to answer this question, but according to my personal observation, the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee will not break away from the Nanjing central government." "Someone asked whether the Japanese side will assist the North China authorities in suppressing the Communists, as Communist activities have been discovered in southern Hebei and Suiyuan. This depends on the development of the actual situation. If the situation becomes increasingly serious, the Japanese military authorities in North China will naturally take this into account for their own responsibilities." "Regarding the issue of the 'Man'-Mongolian border and the Soviet-'Man' conflict, although the situation seems serious recently, I believe that the Soviet Union has no intention of invading 'Manchuria'. Therefore, I expect the situation not to become more serious. However, the Soviet-'Man' border must be demarcated clearly, and the border between Chahar North and Mongolia also needs to be demarcated clearly." "Liu Guitang has nothing to do with the Japanese side, because the Japanese side has no need for him. Li Shouxin also has no relationship with the 'Man' side. That department is a Mongolian troop." However, the visitor asked why Li's department raised the fake "Manchukuo" flag and wore fake "Manchukuo" military uniforms. Doihara did not answer. As for the rumor that Puyi will come to Beiping in March, Doihara firmly denies it.

Organizational Regulations of the Hebei-Chahar Diplomatic Committee The Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee

The Diplomatic Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee will convene a meeting within this week to discuss various diplomatic matters in Hebei and Chahar, as they require further study. The organizational regulations of the committee have been revised by the Political Affairs Committee and announced on the 18th. The original text is as follows: "Article 1: The Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee establishes a Diplomatic Committee for the purpose of studying and handling various diplomatic issues in Hebei, Chahar, Beiping, and Tianjin." "Article 2: The Committee shall have seven to eleven members, who shall be appointed by the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee." "Article 3: The Committee shall have one Chairman, who shall be appointed by the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee from among the members of the Committee. The Chairman shall manage all affairs of the Committee." "Article 4: The Committee shall have the following groups: Group 1 shall be in charge of the Committee's documents, accounting, general affairs, seals, translation, publishing, communication, and other matters. Group 2 shall be in charge of studying and handling diplomatic matters and international intelligence matters." "Article 5: Each group in the preceding article shall have one director and three sections. Each section shall have one section chief, five staff members, and four clerks to handle the affairs of each group." "Article 6: The Committee shall have four secretaries, who shall be in charge of the Committee's confidential affairs in Chinese, English, French, and Japanese." "Article 7: The Committee may have five to seven expert members." "Article 8: The Committee may appoint several consultants, counselors, and advisors." "Article 9: The Committee may employ staff to write documents." "Article 10: The Committee shall hold a meeting every two weeks." "Article 11: When necessary, or upon the proposal of five or more members, the Chairman may convene a special meeting." "Article 12: The Chairman shall be the ex officio chairman of the Committee's meetings. If the Chairman is absent, the members may elect a temporary chairman." "Article 13: The rules of procedure and rules of conduct for the Committee's meetings shall be determined separately." "Article 14: If there are any matters not covered by these regulations, the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee shall revise them." "Article 15: These regulations shall come into effect on the date of their promulgation by the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee." (18th)

Qingdao Executes Drug Offender for the First Time: Prisoner Paraded Through the Streets and Then Tied to the Execution Ground for Execution 78

Qingdao Correspondence: In the era of Japanese administration in Qingdao, opium was sold by public sale, so there were particularly many people addicted to this habit. After our country took over, it was strictly prohibited. Most opium smokers switched to smoking white heroin and other drugs. Also, because there were certain country's ronin secretly selling them, although the authorities strictly prohibited it, this bad habit has not been reduced much. In the past three years, more than 3,000 drug offenders have been arrested and sent to drug rehabilitation centers by the Public Security Bureau. There are still seven or eight hundred drug offenders detained in the center. Since the municipal government was ordered by the central government last year to establish a trial office for violent drug offenders and appointed Secretary General Hu Jiafeng as the director and Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Shize as the deputy director, it was planned to select several drug offenders with serious crimes to be shot to serve as a warning. Initially, fifteen people were selected, and then three were selected from the fifteen. Of these three, two died of illness recently, leaving only the prisoner Ding Yuting. He was tied to the Tuandao execution ground at 2:00 p.m. on the 18th for execution. The investigation revealed that Ding was 26 years old, a native of Yexian County, Shandong Province, and worked as a clerk at the Tiande Shoe Store at No. 60, Xia Sifang Village. He had an addiction to smoking violent drugs on a regular basis. He was arrested by the Public Security Bureau on November 26, 23rd year of the Republic, and sent to the drug rehabilitation center to be forced to quit. After being issued a certificate of abstinence, he signed a statement that he was willing to be executed if he relapsed. Unexpectedly, the prisoner did not think of changing his ways and changed his name to Li Mingzhi and still frequented morphine houses. On February 1st of last year, he was discovered by the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau. Because there was no concrete evidence of smoking, he was sent back to his hometown after being detained. Before long, he sneaked back to Qingdao and relapsed. On September 25th of last year, he bought two small packages of heroin for two jiao of foreign currency at a morphine house on Wulu Road in Taitong Town. He was searched and found by the Fourth Branch of the Public Security Bureau and sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. After confirming the facts, he was transferred to the trial office for violent drug offenders of the municipal government for trial. He confessed to relapsing without denial and was immediately sentenced to death. The case was submitted by the municipal government to the Military Affairs Commission for instructions and approval. On the afternoon of the 18th of this month, at 2:00 p.m., Deputy Director Wang Shize of the Trial Office presented the prisoner to verify his identity. He was tied up in a car, and officers and police of the special task force were sent to guard the car in full armor. Because it was the first time a drug offender was shot, the Public Security Bureau paraded him through the major streets of the city for the public to watch and to serve as a warning. The viewers along the way blocked the roads. After parading for more than an hour, he arrived at the Tuandao execution ground and was executed by shooting. The supervising officer was Shen Guojun, the third section chief of the Public Security Bureau. After the shooting, more than 200 drug offenders in the Tuandao drug rehabilitation center were called out to watch the execution. After Section Chief Shen strictly reprimanded the drug offenders, the Public Security Bureau prepared a coffin for burial. (18th)

Changshu: Fish Tax Investigation Reveals Embezzlement 79

Hupu Town, located near the riverside, is a famous fishing ground in Jiangsu Province. The fish market is very prosperous every spring and summer, but the amount of tax revenue is huge. There was originally a fish ticket tax office there, which levied a tax of three cents per ticket. Unexpectedly, most of this tax revenue was embezzled by the fish merchants. After citizen Wang Yu filed a complaint with the province, the Finance Department sent Wang Zijun to Changshu to investigate. They found that the allegations were indeed true. As a result, the fish merchants were ordered to return all the tax revenue they had embezzled over the years, totaling more than 20,000 yuan. Now, the local citizens believe that this tax revenue was originally designated for local construction, and they request that it still be designated for repairing the dike in Hupukou after it is returned.

Civil Education Institutions Ordered to Close 80

In order to implement civic training and concentrate economic talents, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has ordered all civil education institutions in all counties of the province to be closed. It has also been decided that all counties south of the Yangtze River must stop working before March 15th. All expenses will be used for training expenses, and all personnel in the various institutions will be recommended by the county to preside over public training. The Education Bureau here has been ordered to inform the various institutions to comply and close down, and all equipment and miscellaneous items of the institutions will be taken care of by personnel dispatched by the Education Bureau.

Wuxi: Spring Snowfall Affects Broad Beans and Wheat 81

Since the beginning of spring in this county, the weather has been gloomy and cold, with roads covered in rain and snow. On the 30th of last month, there was heavy fog. From 7 PM the night before last, dense fog again engulfed the area, obstructing the air. Within five steps, one could not distinguish pedestrians, and a foul smell permeated the fog, making people susceptible to illness. It gradually dissipated by yesterday morning, and the weather turned colder. According to the weather report from the second-class weather station in this county, there was heavy fog on the morning of the 17th, with precipitation of 0.3 millimeters. The total precipitation this month is 21.2 millimeters. The most frequent wind direction is north-northeast. The highest temperature was 4.1 degrees Celsius (39.4 degrees Fahrenheit), and the lowest temperature was 2.5 degrees Celsius (36.5 degrees Fahrenheit). This kind of heavy fog is particularly unfavorable for broad beans and wheat in the surrounding countryside. Spring weather requires gentle breezes and warm sunshine for crops to thrive. With gloomy cold and heavy fog, a poor harvest is inevitable in the future. On the morning of the 18th, the weather was still cold, with floating clouds covering the sky, as if it were winter. By 11 AM, snowflakes fluttered down, followed by snow pellets. By 2 PM in the afternoon, heavy snow was falling, and soon, the mountains, forests, and houses were all covered in white.

Hangzhou: Reorganization of Salt Fields in Zhejiang Province 82

In order to reorganize the salt fields in Zhejiang province, the Ministry of Finance has specially ordered the establishment of an inspection and design committee for the Zhejiang salt region by the Salt Affairs Inspection General Office. Zeng Yangfeng has been appointed as the head of the committee, and Yang Xingli, Huang Boye, and Wu Shangzhi as members. They arrived in Hangzhou on the fast train on the evening of the 17th. Yesterday (the 18th), they went to the Salt Transport Office to discuss the inspection procedures and the reorganization of the field production, deployment of tax police, and expenses with the Salt Commissioner Zhou Zonghua. It was decided that the reorganization of the Yuyao field, which had already begun, and the Daishan and former fields should continue. The research on various ongoing tasks was quite detailed. The 18 small salt fields that should be abolished will also be implemented after the reorganization. The total cost will be more than 3.6 million yuan.

Ningbo: Resignation of the Head of Zhenhai People's Education Center 83

Xu Deyang, the head of the Zhenhai County People's Education Center, was appointed to his current position by the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education in March of the 20th year. For the past five years, he has been very diligent in his duties and has achieved remarkable results, which has been widely praised. However, due to the difficulty in handling affairs recently, Director Xu suddenly had the idea of resigning and has submitted a request to the Provincial Department of Education for dismissal. It is unknown whether his request will be approved.

Bengbu: Repairing the Huai River Dike Before the Spring Flood 84

As the spring flood season is approaching, the Anhui Provincial Government believes that the Huai River dike repair project cannot be relaxed in the slightest. Recently, it has sent separate telegrams to the commissioners of Si County and Fuyang in northern Anhui, urging them to strictly supervise the counties, enlist more laborers, and work hard to repair the dike. It also ordered that at the beginning of the construction, capable personnel should be selected to serve as inspectors of the Huai River dike project, regularly inspect the dikes within their jurisdiction, and work with personnel sent by the construction department to expedite the completion of the project as soon as possible. Upon receiving the order, the three commissioners immediately urged the counties to work hard on the repairs.
