Second Anniversary of the New Life Movement: Celebrations Held by All Sectors: Grand Commemorative Meeting Held in the City Chamber of Commerce Yesterday Morning; Inspection of Government Agencies and Broadcast Speeches in the Afternoon 85

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, to commemorate the second anniversary of the New Life Movement, convened representatives from all sectors at the City Chamber of Commerce auditorium at 9:00 AM on the 19th to hold a commemorative meeting, which adjourned at 11:00 AM. In the afternoon, government agencies were inspected to review the results of implementing the New Life Movement, and directors Pan Gongzhan and Wu Xingya gave broadcast speeches. Details are as follows:

Enthusiastic Branches: The commemorative meeting was very well attended. Those present included instructor Wu Tiecheng, the presidium of Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Yang Hu, Yu Hongjun, Zhang Shouyong, general affairs director Jiang Hao, reception director Lu Jingshi, discipline director Cai Jingjun, as well as representatives from various government agencies and organizations Huang Xuchu, Zhu Xuefan, Yu Zhenhui, Lin Kecong, Lin Xianwen, Xia Huan, Li Shiyong, students and boy scouts from various schools, and all staff members of the New Life Movement Association, totaling more than 2,000 people.

Venue Arrangement: At the entrance of the venue, military police from the Chinese-administered areas of the city were stationed, with about a dozen guards. On both sides of the passage, boy scouts from the City Chamber of Commerce stood guard. At the entrance, staff members of the New Life Movement Association assisted the boy scouts in receiving guests. Boy scouts also maintained order inside the venue. The venue was covered with various slogans. In front of the rostrum was a bamboo cloth banner with the inscription "Shanghai All Circles Commemorate the Second Anniversary of the New Life Movement." All arrangements were extremely simple and solemn.

Chairman's Address: After the ceremonial procedures at 9:00 AM, Chairman Zhang Taoyong delivered the opening address, stating that the implementation of the New Life Movement has been in effect for two years. We firmly believe that the New Life Movement is the only way to save China at present. Therefore, since its implementation, it has been vigorously promoted and has become widespread throughout the country. The essence of the New Life Movement is to seek the productionization, artisticization, and militarization of life. Because of the current moral decline of the Chinese nation, militarization must be sought to save it. Because of the lack of rules in the spirit, artisticization must be sought to save it. China must also seek productionization to save it from economic decline. Such methods seek the revival of the Chinese nation.

Wu's Instructions: Instructor Wu Tiecheng then gave instructions, stating that the New Life Movement has been advocated by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for two years. Because it deeply meets the needs of the times and is a major plan for the revival of the nation, it has become a prevailing trend, and the whole country has followed suit. In recent times, various movements in Chinese history have emerged one after another, but their effects have either only been seen in the advocacy of a few patriots, without being followed by the general public, or have only been a temporary excitement, without lasting power. The New Life Movement is different. The New Life Movement is the driving force for promoting new policies, reviving the nation, and advancing all cultural construction in China. The basic points of the New Life Movement lie in the spirit of "If one day is new, make it new again, and keep it new day after day," as well as the determination of "All kinds of things in the past are as if dead yesterday, and all kinds of things in the future are as if born today," sweeping away all the sluggish and decadent customs at the bottom of society, and eradicating all the decadent habits deeply rooted in people's hearts, in order to cultivate a new habit of perseverance, uprightness, unyielding, and upward struggle, so that the lives of the people of the whole country can become more rational, scientific, productive, revolutionary, militarized, modernized, and artistic. Therefore, in the future, this New Life Movement must be universally applied to the entire nation, penetrating the general public, so that it can become a habit, and the revival of the nation can be expected in the near future.

Wu's Speech: Wu Xingya then gave a speech, stating that the New Life Movement has been popular for two weeks under the guidance of President Chiang. Because the New Life Movement is a key plan to save the country and the nation, those of us who are responsible for promoting it should strive hard. On this second anniversary, we should first conduct a review of our work. In the past two years, from this city to the whole country, to what extent has the promotion of the New Life Movement reached? Second, self-reflection: Those of us who are responsible for promoting the movement should practice what we preach. Can we abide by all the rules of the New Life Movement? In terms of promotion, can we fulfill our responsibilities? Third, our beliefs: Are our beliefs in the New Life Movement firm? Fourth, our future direction: We should look around at the current environment in China and determine the direction of our actions. Madam Zhou Shang also gave a speech, which is omitted here.

Afternoon Inspection: Yesterday afternoon, Yang Hu, Cai Jingjun, Zhang Shouyong, Lu Jingshi, and other directors of the association set off in four groups to inspect the implementation of the Three-fold life (productionization, artisticization, and militarization) in various government agencies. The first group, led by Lu Jingshi and accompanied by Hu Tianseng, inspected the City Party Headquarters, the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Hydrographic Office, the Security Office, the Party Headquarters of the Security Office, the Bureau of Finance, the Bureau of Land, the Garrison Headquarters, the Second Special District Court, the Third High Court Branch, and the Trademark Bureau. The second group, led by Yang Hu and accompanied by Zhu Jiarang, Chen Jie, and Wang Jiyi, inspected the Municipal Government's Bureau of Social Affairs, Bureau of Public Utilities, Bureau of Education, Bureau of Public Works, Bureau of Health, the Party Headquarters of the Two Roads (railways), the First Special District Court, and the Second High Court Branch. All detachments were able to conscientiously fulfill the regulations.

Zhang's Speech: Yesterday was the second anniversary of the New Life Movement. In addition to convening a commemorative meeting of representatives from all sectors at the City Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association also conducted a general inspection of all public service agencies in the city. Zhang Shouzhu, the director of the association and president of Guanghua University, was the inspector for the third group. Afterwards, they gave a speech to all the staff members of the bureau in the auditorium. The original speech is as follows: Comrades, usually when the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association holds directors' meetings, many matters are decided to be handled by the Public Security Bureau. The New Life Movement Promotion Association has become a hollow organization. Only the Public Security Bureau is the actual promoting agency of the New Life Movement. I have seen that the work and management of the various departments of your bureau are very effective, and the spirit of work is very good. This shows the efforts of everyone in promoting the New Life Movement. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau is truly worthy of being a model for Shanghai. From this, we can see the spirit of rectifying police administration and implementing the New Life Movement. I usually think that the life of a criminal in prison is the most tragic thing in the world. Therefore, I especially went to your bureau's detention center to take a look. Although the place of your bureau's detention center is not very large, it is very clean inside, and there is no smell. The life of the prisoners is also comfortable. This is really a rare thing. Everyone must know that it is better to prevent trouble before it happens than to eliminate it after it has happened. Everyone has the responsibility to enforce the law. Now, everyone is promoting the New Life Movement, and if you use the method of moral persuasion instead of punishment, the masses will be easily moved and accepted. In this way, the New Life Movement promoted by Mr. Chiang will surely be carried out without hindrance and become the foundation of national revival. In the past, when I attended a financial conference, Mr. Dai Jitao once said, "The situation of Chinese government offices is the same as that of the local bailiffs and tax card checkers." I was very moved when I heard this sentence. Could it be that the evils of society are all the evils of officials? Therefore, the promotion of the New Life Movement must first of all enable everyone to lead by example. Today, when I came to your bureau to see the achievements of the New Life Movement, I felt that everyone's spirit was very good and their work was very serious. Everyone can truly be said to be leading by example. What everyone is doing is the foundation of national revival. I run schools and educate young people, which is also the foundation of the country. I am sixty-one years old this year. I think that we old people should follow the young people. Old people can only talk about their experiences, and the implementation still depends on young people. I am very happy to see you young comrades today, so I say these words from my heart to contribute to everyone. If everyone still thinks that what the old man said is worth listening to, and not "old hat," then I hope everyone will take what this old man said as a reference. Finally, I wish everyone good health, work hard for the country, and promote the New Life Movement.

Wang Jingwei Went to Europe Yesterday for Medical Treatment: It Is Only Temporary and He Will Return Once Recovered; Madam Wang Did Not Travel Due to Illness 86

According to the Central News Agency, Wang Jingwei, the chairman of the Central Political Committee who was recovering from injuries in Shanghai, took the North German Lloyd ship "Nassau" to Europe yesterday for medical treatment. Mr. Wang's trip is only temporary. Those traveling with him include Zeng Zhongming, Chen Yaozu, and Dr. Zhuer. The details are as follows:

Departure Yesterday: News of Wang's departure for medical treatment has been circulating for a long time, but those around him have denied it. Therefore, it was not confirmed until after he boarded the ship yesterday afternoon. Zeng Zhongming still denied the news of Wang's transfer for medical treatment fifteen minutes before Wang's departure. This shows the secrecy of Wang's whereabouts. Wang, accompanied by Zeng Zhongming, left his residence on Anhe Temple Road at 2:45 PM yesterday in a Beijing Municipal Police registration car No. 490 and a Shanghai Concession registration car No. 11180. At 3:10 PM, he arrived at the New Customs Wharf. Along the way and near the New Customs Wharf, detectives from the Public Concession Police Department were specially dispatched to escort him. After Wang arrived at the New Customs Wharf, he immediately boarded the Maoxin small ferry to the Eleventh Floating Pontoon and boarded the "Nassau" ship. At 4:30 PM, the ship set sail for Europe. Only Central Committee Member Chu Minyi and his wife, Legislative Committee Member Lin Baisheng and his wife, Wang's secretary Lin Ruheng, and more than twenty reporters from various newspapers went to the wharf to see him off.

Madam Stays in Shanghai: Those who accompanied Wang abroad yesterday included former Railway official Zeng Zhongming and former Deputy Director of the Jinpu Railway Chen Yaozu. Foreign advisor Tang Liangli also traveled to Europe on the same ship for investigation. Dr. Noel, who happened to be returning to Germany for business, specially accompanied Wang so that all treatments on the ship could proceed as usual. It was also heard that German doctor Professor Sauerbruch, the world's only expert in wound treatment, will be visited by Wang after arriving in Europe for consultation. As for Madam Chen Bijun, Wang's wife, she has been suffering from a severe cold since the 13th or 14th, and doctors diagnosed her with pneumonia, which was very serious. The fever only slightly subsided on the 17th or 18th, and her condition only slightly improved, but she was still unable to get out of bed. Therefore, Madam Wang did not travel with him yesterday, nor did she see Wang off on the ship.

Good Spirits: Wang wore a gray-blue long robe and a black mandarin jacket yesterday. When he got out of the car at the New Customs Wharf, he held a cane in one hand and a felt hat in the other, and was supported by people on the left and right as he boarded the ship. Wang's face looked slightly pale, but he was still plump and in good spirits, and his gait was also healthy.

Injuries and Symptoms: According to Wang's entourage, Wang was assassinated on November 1st last year and suffered three bullet wounds. One was in his left arm, and the bullet passed through the skin and flesh. After treatment, it completely healed. However, one bullet in his back, right above the upper left side of the ribs, was taken out once on the day of the injury. After arriving in Shanghai on the 21st of the same month, he underwent a second operation on the 29th, but it has not been removed. Even now, it still hurts from time to time. As for the bullet in his left cheek, although it was removed at the Central Hospital, it injured the muscles and nerves too much. Until now, the muscles in his left cheek cannot move freely, and his mouth can only open to the width of one finger. He still needs to undergo electrotherapy every day to gradually restore the muscles. This is the general situation of Wang's injuries since the assassination. Wang also suffered from diabetes and gallstones. After November 1st, due to excessive blood loss from the injuries, it was repeatedly triggered. Dr. Noel, who has been treating Wang, paid special attention to this, and fortunately it did not worsen. However, since the source of the disease has not been removed, medicine is indispensable. In addition, his whole body was weakened after the serious injuries, which affected his heart, resulting in a new symptom of intermittent pulse. In recent days, the intermittent phenomenon often reached seven or eight times per minute. This is also the general situation of Wang's old illnesses triggered by new wounds after the assassination.

Telegram to Meet Hu: According to Wang's entourage, transferring to another place for medical treatment has long been advocated by the doctors treating Wang's injuries. Later, upon hearing the news of Mr. Hu Hanmin's return to China, it was first said that Hu would arrive in Hong Kong on the 19th on the original ship and come to Shanghai. Later, there was news that he would rest in Hong Kong for a few days before going north. Wang wanted to wait for Hu to come north in order to meet him, so the transfer for medical treatment was repeatedly postponed, and this news was not announced. On the 8th of this month, Wang sent a telegram to Hu, explaining this intention. The telegram contained the words "Originally scheduled to transfer for medical treatment at the end of last month, but repeatedly changed the travel date in order to wait for instruction," and asked when Hu could come. He then received a reply telegram from Hu on the 10th, which stated, "Since entering Guangdong, I have been frequently suffering from colds due to the changing climate. The doctors all say that my physical strength cannot withstand the cold weather in the north, and I still need to rest for a while." Wang, realizing that Hu could not come immediately, followed the doctor's advice and transferred for medical treatment first. According to a representative of the Guangdong side stationed in Shanghai, the procedures for Wang's departure were completed half a month ago. It was originally planned to go abroad earlier, but it was delayed in order to wait for a meeting with Hu Zhantang, the chairman of the Central Standing Committee. Now that Hu cannot come immediately, he will leave first. He may be able to meet Hu when passing through Hong Kong.

Short-Term Trip Abroad: Wang will reportedly land in Marseille and then transfer to Germany. However, his entourage said that it has not yet been decided where Wang will land in Europe. This trip is purely for medical treatment and there are no other opinions to be expressed. According to Wang, this trip will be very short, probably no more than a few months. Once his injuries and illnesses have been slightly relieved, he will return to China. Due to his illness, all visits and social interactions along the way will be declined.

Formal Agreement Signed for Nanping Section Loan: 10 Million Yuan Each for Construction Funds and Material Purchases; Procedures for Loan Distribution and Material Purchases Have Been Stipulated 87

10 Million Yuan Each for Construction Funds and Material Purchases Procedures for Loan Distribution and Material Purchases Have Been Stipulated The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Company is extending the railway from Nanchang to Pingxiang. The Ministry of Railways issued a second phase of railway construction bonds of 27 million yuan on February 1st to borrow 10 million yuan each from Shanghai banking groups and Otto Wolff Steel Works for construction funds and material purchases. The chairman of the railway company, Zeng Yangfu, negotiated with the banking groups and submitted the agreement to the Ministry of Railways for approval. The agreement was formally signed in Shanghai a few days ago. The details are as follows:

Construction Funds and Material Purchases The Ministry of Railways issued a second phase of railway construction bonds of 27 million yuan and allocated them to the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Company for the extension of the railway from Nanchang to Pingxiang. The chairman of the company, Zeng Yangfu, was responsible for contacting the Shanghai banking groups represented by the Bank of China and the German Otto Wolff Steel Works. It was decided that both the construction funds and the materials would be changed to 10 million yuan each. The interest rate and repayment period of the loan were immediately discussed, and a draft contract was drawn up. Zeng carried it to Beijing and submitted it to the Ministry of Railways for approval. Then, a few days ago, he came to Shanghai and invited representatives from various banks to formally sign the agreement.

Formal Agreement Has Been Signed The agreement was signed on the 11th of this month. Zeng Yangfu represented the Ministry of Railways. The representatives from the banking groups included Huo Laishu from the Bank of China, Zhang Peishen from the Bank of Communications, Wu Yunzhai from the Jincheng Bank, Zhu Runsheng from the Farmers Bank of China, Wang Zhixin from the Xinhua Bank, Wu Shiyi from the Jiangxi Yumin Bank, Song Ziliang from the China Construction Finance Corporation, Shen Shuyu from the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, and Wolff from the German Steel Works. A total of two general agreements were signed. One copy was held by the Ministry of Railways and the other by the banking groups. The agreement for the purchase of materials was also signed in the same format, with an attached price list, detailing the prices of various materials required.

Distribution of Construction Funds The total amount of construction funds borrowed is 10 million yuan, which is borrowed by eight banks including the Bank of China. The Bank of China has the most, with 3.2 million yuan. The Bank of Communications and the Farmers Bank of China each have 2 million yuan. The Jincheng Bank has 1 million yuan. The Xinhua Bank, the Jiangxi Yumin Bank, and the China Construction Finance Corporation each have 500,000 yuan. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau has 300,000 yuan. The funds will be released to the banking groups as needed when the project progresses. The material purchase is also limited to 10 million yuan. The steel rails, sleepers, bridges, locomotives, telegraphs, telephones, and other materials needed during the project will be supplied by the factory. However, the order must be placed before June 15th of this year, and the factory must deliver the goods within eight weeks of receiving the order. The factory must also notify the banking groups of the total number of materials ordered within one week.

Repayment Period The agreement stipulates that the construction funds will be repaid in five years, with an annual interest rate of one percent, starting from January of this year. Interest will be settled and paid on June 30th and December 31st each year. The material purchase funds will be repaid in six years, with an annual interest rate of seven percent, and interest will also be paid on June 12th and December each year. The repayment method stipulates that after the railway section is open to traffic and in operation, 20 percent of the net profit will be allocated each year for the banking groups to distribute and repay the banking groups and the German factory. The banks receive two-thirds of the total amount, and the German factory receives one-third, until the debt is cleared. The income of the railway must be deposited in the Bank of China at any time for accounting and payment.

Announcement by the Banking Association: Checks Are Exempt from Stamp Duty 88

The Shanghai Banking Association announced yesterday that the National Government has issued an order exempting checks from stamp duty. Yesterday, it separately notified all banks in the association and published a notice in the newspaper to alert bank depositors. The details of this matter are as follows:

Request Process The Shanghai Banking Association previously received a letter from the Tianjin Banking Association, stating that the new stamp tax law stipulates that checks must be affixed with stamps, fearing that it would be like "exhausting the fish to collect taxes." It repeatedly requested the government to temporarily exempt them. However, on September 1st of last year, when the new stamp tax law went into effect, it had not yet received a reply. Therefore, on August 31st of last year, it announced to bank depositors that before the request for exemption was approved, it would temporarily comply with the law and all checks would be stamped.

Contact with the Tax Bureau On February 10th of this year, the National Government ordered that checks be temporarily exempted from stamp duty. It is heard that the banking sector had contacted the Stamp Tax Bureau. The bureau also stated that since the order had been promulgated, it should be followed. Based on this reply, the Banking Association notified the banks in the association to comply with the order and published a notice in the newspaper to alert all sectors.

Notice to All Sectors The Banking Association issued an announcement yesterday, stating, "Regarding the stamp tax on checks, this association has previously submitted a request to the legislative and financial authorities, earnestly requesting exemption. Now, the Legislative Yuan has reviewed and approved this case, allowing temporary exemption, and the National Government promulgated an order on February 10th of this year, which should be followed. In addition to notifying the banks in the association for investigation and handling, we hereby publish a notice in the newspaper to alert all sectors."

Goldsmith Industry Requests Modification of Regulations; Ministry of Finance Rejects, Guild Decides to Petition in the Capital 89

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Goldsmith Industry Guild, regarding the issue of gold and silver fineness, has repeatedly requested the Ministry of Finance to amend the management regulations. Yesterday, the guild received a response from the Ministry of Finance, document number Qian Zi 8630. The response stated: "Received and noted. Upon investigation, the preparation of alloys does not require the use of powerful boilers or oxygen smelting. Moreover, the melting point of alloys is consistently lower than that of their individual components, eliminating any difficulty in melting. The Ministry has already ordered the Central Mint to prepare and supply these alloys. The goldsmith industry can purchase them at any time, ensuring no work difficulties. The request to amend the management regulations to allow the continued manufacturing of products with the same composition is hereby denied. Please adhere to the Ministry's previous decision." After receiving the response, the guild immediately convened an executive committee meeting and decided to petition in the capital after the National Goldsmith Industry Representatives Conference is held.

Tobacco Exchange Industry Proposes Setting Exchange Regulations 90

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, the Shanghai Branch of the Tobacco Exchange Industry Guild, in view of the government's currency reform which offers convenience to various industries, and reports from members highlighting the significant impact on their business, specially convened an interim meeting yesterday of the supervisory and executive committees in the southern district of the city. The key proposals are listed below:

* At the beginning of the new subsidiary currency's circulation, counterfeit coins have already been discovered in the market. The guild should petition the municipal government to order an investigation and crackdown, and notify members to be vigilant and avoid losses.

* The circulation of subsidiary currency affects exchange rates. If the exchange rate is not standardized, it will be even more difficult to maintain business. The guild should petition the authorities to set the exchange rate at 3,000 [cash] per legal tender dollar to rectify the situation and prevent competition.

* Exchange transactions have always been a major business for the industry, with profits derived from exchanging silver dollars for copper coins or silver dimes. Based on the market rate for such exchanges, several dozens of cash are deducted per dollar. Now that subsidiary currency is decimalized, if no handling fee is stipulated, arbitrary price suppression would easily cause disputes and undermine the currency system. The guild should petition the authorities to stipulate that for each legal tender dollar exchanged for subsidiary currency, a handling fee of one cent should be allowed, with no arbitrary deductions permitted.

* Exchange transactions have always been the primary business of this industry. Other businesses receive copper coins and silver dimes, which are exchanged into silver dollars, and residents exchange silver dollars for silver dimes and copper coins, all through tobacco exchange shops. Now that the currency system is reformed and decimalization is promoted, other businesses can also engage in exchange transactions. If this is not restricted, the source of exchange transactions will be cut off, endangering the livelihoods of this industry, as well as affecting peddlers. Vegetable market peddlers, for example, sell for silver dimes and copper coins, which are then exchanged for silver dollars at tobacco exchange shops, typically with an additional 20 or 30 cash added. Now that other businesses are also engaging in exchange transactions, their exchange rates will inevitably be higher than those of tobacco exchange shops. If tobacco exchange shops offer an exchange rate of 3,000 cash, they will charge 3,020 or 3,030 cash when receiving silver dimes and copper coins from peddlers. Due to the higher exchange rates offered by other businesses, tobacco exchange shops will inevitably raise their purchasing rates, thereby harming the interests of peddlers. To protect the industry's business and maintain the livelihood of the people, the guild should petition the authorities to establish regulations for exchange transactions and allow for exclusive operation.

* The delay in the guild's affairs has failed the trust of its members. Members are facing dangerous business conditions, previously due to disordered commodity prices and recently due to the impact of the currency system. It is urgent to find ways to protect the industry, take proactive measures, and avoid complacency, which would lead to self-destruction. The committees should be urged to expedite the proceedings to revitalize the business and safeguard the livelihoods of members.

* The establishment of branch offices in the northern and southern districts was approved by the members' congress. Registration with the competent authorities should be completed. However, many days have passed without approval. The guild should promptly urge for the approval to complete the procedures and facilitate progress.

The above matters were resolved to be submitted to a plenary meeting of the executive and supervisory committees for a public decision.

Tang Leang-Li Departs Yesterday to Europe for News Industry Observation; First to Germany, Then Traveling England, France, and Italy; For Four or Five Months, Also Conducts International Publicity 98

Tang Leang-Li, a Minister-level advisor to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs dispatched to Europe to observe the news industry and conduct international publicity, departed yesterday afternoon with Wang Jingwei, Chairman of the Central Political Council, aboard the North German Lloyd's ship "Gneisenau." Mr. Tang is one of the leading English writers in the country. He studied in England and Germany for many years. His books, "China in Revolt" and "The Foundations of Modern China," have long been praised by people in Europe and America. After returning to China in 1930, he founded the English-language magazine "The People's Tribune." In 1933, he was hired as an advisor to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, overseeing foreign publicity affairs. He has published "China's Own Critics", "Wang Ching-Wei's China's Problems and Their Solution", "Reconstructing China", and "China's Railways Today". This month, he published "The New Social Order in China" and "China's New Currency System". Currently being compiled are "A History of Chinese Transportation and Its Organization" by Chu Chia-Hua and "China's Finances" by H.H. Kung. His trip abroad is in response to an invitation from the German Foreign Ministry last autumn. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs of China considered it feasible and assigned him the task of observing the news industry and conducting publicity. Mr. Tang will first go to Germany, then travel to England, France, and Italy, continuing to publish "The People's Tribune."

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's Instructions on Stamp Duty for Leases 102

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce replied to Lixing Paint Store yesterday with instructions on how to affix stamp duty to leases: "In reply, we have received your letter of the 18th of this month inquiring about the stamp duty for leases. We have taken note of it. The reply is as follows:

Your leases, you say, did not have stamp duty affixed in 1934 or 1935. The new Stamp Duty Law came into effect on September 1, 1935. Therefore, stamp duty on leases before September 1, 1935, should be handled according to the amount stipulated in the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Duty, affixing one dime per year.

Although the two years of missed stamp duty were within the period of the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Duty, the Stamp Duty Inspection Office took away the leases in November, at which time the new Stamp Duty Law had already come into effect and the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Duty had been abolished. Therefore, the penalties for missed stamp duty should be handled in accordance with the penalty provisions of Article 18 of the new Stamp Duty Law, which is 10 to 30 times the amount of tax owed. For example, if the lease should have been affixed with one dime each year, the penalty for missed stamp duty is 3 yuan, calculated at 30 times the amount. For two years of missed stamp duty, the combined penalty is 6 yuan.

Using a lease to collect rent is the same as using a house ticket to collect rent, both being methods for landlords to collect money from tenants. However, a house ticket is issued by the landlord to the tenant, while a lease is issued by the tenant to the landlord. Therefore, the issuer of a house ticket is the landlord, while the issuer of a lease is the tenant. Therefore, the responsibility for affixing stamp duty to a lease, and the responsibility for missing stamp duty, should be borne by the tenant.

The stamp duty for this year's leases should be affixed annually at two dimes each, in accordance with Article 16, Clause 10 of the Stamp Duty Law."

Villagers of Hejiajiao Petition for Postponement of House Tax Collection 104

Villagers of Hejiajiao in the French Concession of Western Shanghai are requesting the Municipal Finance Bureau to postpone the collection of house tax. Four representatives, Wang Guangrun, Xing Pengju, Yang Xingchu, and Yang Shuguo, were elected by the entire village to depart for the Municipal Government yesterday morning with a petition. The reasons are as follows: Hejiajiao in the French Concession is a purely rural village with over 200 households living in simple, low-lying houses inherited from their ancestors, merely sheltering themselves from the wind and rain. The population of over 1,000 people mostly makes a living by farming, with some engaged in industry. However, in recent years, natural disasters and man-made calamities have followed one after another, and they have been affected by the urban economic downturn. Farmers have suffered from poor harvests and low prices, and industrial and commercial enterprises have failed. Living at home, they are in dire straits, barely able to feed themselves. The Municipal Finance Bureau's collection of house tax is truly difficult to comply with. They jointly request the government to allow a postponement of the collection to alleviate the suffering of the people. At 9:30 AM, the first group of petitioners arrived at the Municipal Government. The second group of people were stopped by the police at the Seventh District Public Security Gate, but the police chief escorted the four representatives to the Municipal Government, where the mayor sent Director Yuan of the Second Section to receive them. He promised to submit the petition to the mayor and assured them that he would convey the difficulties of the farmers. The representatives were satisfied and returned to the village with the people. It was already past 3 PM.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Sues Shareholders of Yikang and Yongxing Money Shops; Over 4,000 Yuan Owed to Exhibition Hall Fund; Should Be Cleared by Shareholders Yan Ruling et al. 106

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce is suing the shareholders of the Yikang and Yongxing money shops for owing a total of over 4,000 yuan to the Chamber's Exhibition Hall Library Fund. Yesterday, Zheng Zenan, director of the Chamber's Finance Department, filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court in his capacity as legal representative, requesting the shareholders of the two shops to clear the debts in full. The original complaint states: "For the matter of owed deposits, requesting joint and several repayment. The defendants Yan Ruling, Wu Jincheng, Peng Guinian, Xu Baoyuan, You Lianzeng, and Chen Sisheng are all shareholders of the Yikang Fengji Money Shop. The defendants Chen Dizhou, Yu Zhendong, Guo Ruoliang, Chen Zhongchi, and Chen Meibo are all shareholders of the Yongxing Money Shop. The plaintiff deposited 1,500 silver taels of standard silver, calculated at 715 [yuan] per tael, equivalent to 2,097.90 yuan, in each of the Yongxing and Yikang Fengji Money Shops as basic funds for the Chamber's Commodity Exhibition Hall Library. However, the Yongxing and Yikang money shops went bankrupt one after another in the first half of last year, and under the guise of liquidation, they have delayed repayment of the plaintiff's deposits. After repeated demands, Yongxing Money Shop only paid 400 yuan on May 6 of the same year, with the remaining amount still outstanding. This amount is a public fund of the plaintiff's Commodity Exhibition Hall Library, and it is not appropriate to allow it to remain outstanding. As of the end of December 1935, Yikang Money Shop owed the plaintiff 2,307.69 yuan, and Yongxing Money Shop owed the plaintiff 1,881.39 yuan. Therefore, we specially request your court to order the defendants Yan Ruling, Wu Jincheng, Peng Guinian, Xu Baoyuan, You Lianzeng, and Chen Sisheng to jointly and severally repay the plaintiff 2,307.69 yuan, plus interest at 1% per annum from January 1, 1936, until the date of repayment, and to order the defendants Chen Dizhou, Yu Zhendong, Guo Ruoliang, Chen Zhongchi, and Chen Meibo to jointly and severally repay the plaintiff 1,881.39 yuan, plus interest at 1% per annum from January 1, 1936, until the date of repayment. The litigation costs should be borne by the defendants for the sake of public convenience. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court for review."

Refining Industry After Changing Systems, Abandoning Non-Monthly Settlement Customers 107

The Shanghai Refining Industry Guild, after receiving orders from the Silk and Satin Industry and the Electric Silk Weaving Industry Guilds to change its system, abolished the old method of pricing per piece of silk from the Spring Festival of this year and adopted the method of calculating length by the metric system, grading and pricing, and establishing a standard public scale. It was approved by the Social Affairs Bureau. However, the Silk and Satin Industry Guild did not agree to the monthly settlement. The Refining Industry believes that credit conditions are extremely tight at this time and suffered huge losses last year, making it impossible to extend the credit period. After several days of meetings and discussions, they decided to abandon transactions with customers who cannot settle monthly.

The current estimate by the auction house is only $3,033 in national currency, which is too low. Fire at Guangguang Electric Factory 113

Yuan Zhangquan, a native of Ningbo, opened the Guangguang Electric Factory at No. 6, 3rd floor, Deran Lane, Jubolai Road, French Concession, manufacturing various bulbs (i.e., small light bulbs) for flashlights. He employed 50 to 60 workers and the business was prosperous on weekdays. After investigation, the fire brigade's Western personnel found that the factory had not obtained a special business license from the French Municipal Council, and the fire-fighting equipment was incomplete, nor had it been reported to the fire brigade for inspection. Sun Chunsheng Declares Bankruptcy But Has No Assets to be Taken Over; Account Books Have Been Taken Away and the Residence Rented to a Portuguese; The Administrator Prosecutes Sun for Fraudulent Bankruptcy – Sun Even Published an Absurd Announcement of “Leaving Shanghai to Return Home” in the Newspaper – 114

Jin Xing Real Estate Company at No. 505, Henan Road, was managed by Sun Chunsheng. Due to heavy debts, creditors such as Henglong Money Exchange petitioned the court to declare bankruptcy. Special Court No. 1 ruled on October 17, 1935, at 9:00 AM, to grant the declaration of bankruptcy and appointed lawyer Liu Shifang and accountant Xie Lin as bankruptcy administrators. Liu and Xie then went to receive Sun's property on October 18 last year, accompanied by a clerk from Special Court No. 1. However, apart from three apprentices and tea servers, there were no other staff in Jin Xing Company. It was claimed that all account books had been taken away by Sun, resulting in no documents being received. It was also found that the stocks of Cathay Bank and Zhongyi Trust Company held by Sun had been transferred to his wife, Shao Yizhen, within one year before and after the bankruptcy. Furthermore, after the bankruptcy administrator was ordered to take over Sun's residence at No. 352, Huade Road, on January 28 this year, a Portuguese named Gao Shida suddenly came forward, claiming that the house had been leased to him by Sun on May 1 last year for a monthly rent of $150 for a term of ten years, and presented receipts for the payment of three years' rent of $5,400 as proof. All these acts violated Articles 154, 2, and 3 of the Bankruptcy Law regarding fraudulent bankruptcy. In order to prevent such evil practices in the future, lawyer Liu and accountant Xie, in their capacity as bankruptcy administrators, filed a criminal private prosecution against Sun Chunsheng with Special Court No. 1. Because Sun's whereabouts were unknown, they requested a warrant for his arrest in accordance with Articles 84, 5, and 6 of the Criminal Law. The case was heard yesterday afternoon by Judge Xiao Fen in the third criminal court. Sun Chunsheng's wife's appointed lawyer, Tai Fei, appeared in court and stated that Sun was currently in Hangzhou recuperating from a lung disease, and requested an adjournment to allow Sun to appear in court for questioning. Lawyer Liu Shifang immediately stated that it had been found that Sun was actually in Shanghai, employing more than a dozen Japanese as bodyguards, and presented an advertisement published by Sun as proof. The words in the advertisement were extremely absurd. It is copied as follows: "Since the Shanghai war on January 28, the global recession has had an impact, and all industries have been declining day by day. How can the real estate industry be alone? It is necessary to plan day and night to properly restore the difficult situation, resulting in excessive labor and neurasthenia. After careful treatment by Chinese and Western doctors, the illness has worsened. I followed the doctor's advice and left Shanghai to return home to recuperate for a long time. It has been several months since all symptoms have improved. I will return to Shanghai in a few days. This is a preliminary announcement to avoid the concern of relatives and friends." After reading it, Judge Xiao thought that the phrase "leaving Shanghai to return home" was extremely absurd. Could it be that he also wanted to imitate the actions of a traitor? He then asked Lawyer Xiong if he knew about Sun's advertisement. Lawyer Xiong replied that he did not know. Judge Xiao then ordered the case to be adjourned to the 26th to summon Sun to court for further questioning.

Jiangbei Associations Discuss Relief for Unemployed Rickshaw Pullers; Deadline for Registering Unemployed Rickshaw Pullers; Notice of Precautions for Pulling Rickshaws 119

Since its establishment, the joint office of various Jiangbei associations in Shanghai convened its first delegates' meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM to discuss the direction of progress. Due to rain, the number of delegates attending did not reach the legal quorum, so the meeting was changed to a discussion meeting to discuss the problem of relieving unemployed rickshaw pullers. The details are recorded as follows:

Discussion on Relief Yesterday, more than ten delegates attended, including Cheng Xiechun, Liu Zhenqiu, Jin Chunlin, Ge Futian, Zhu Hegao, Xi Renfa, and Song Shixiang. Regarding the problem of relieving unemployed rickshaw pullers, the following was decided: Registration of unemployed rickshaw pullers will begin on the 22nd of this month and end on April 30. Issue a registration notice. Send a letter to the special district rickshaw puller office to introduce unemployed military pullers. The registration locations are designated as follows: A. Jianghuai Shanghai Association at the corner of Zhabei Zhongshan Road and Pushan Road; B. Nantong Association at No. 4, Yongji Lane, North Nicheng Bridge, Xizang Road; C. Jianghuai Association at the back door of Xinpuyu Hall, Huining Road, Nanshi.

Notice of Registration Poor farmers from our hometown come to Shanghai to make a living, mostly with the aim of pulling rickshaws. However, due to the工部局's implementation of the rickshaw puller registration policy, it has already ended. All rickshaw pullers who have not been registered cannot pull rickshaws, and there is no opportunity to apply for registration, resulting in more and more unemployed rickshaw pullers gathering in Shanghai, wandering aimlessly, suffering from hunger and cold, and crying in vain. Our hometown associations have recently sent letters one after another, lamenting their plight and requesting relief, which is very pitiful. Therefore, we have established a joint office to first conduct registration of unemployed rickshaw pullers, so as to count the number of people, and then negotiate with the authorities as a basis for applying for registration and licenses. Moreover, the current number of licensed rickshaw pullers is insufficient to meet the demand, resulting in many vehicles being idle. It is indeed necessary to issue additional licenses and increase the number of rickshaw pullers. All our fellow villagers who urgently need to pull rickshaws but have no rickshaws to pull must come to register according to the dates and locations listed above (see above), so that they can have rickshaws to pull and will not wander in a foreign land. Please do not delay.

Precautions for Pulling Rickshaws When you are pulling a rickshaw, you must remember the street names and pay attention to the traffic lights on the road. Always listen to the instructions of the police to control traffic and abide by the road regulations. You cannot run in the middle of the road, you should walk close to the left side of the road. When pulling a rickshaw, you must form a single line and cannot run parallel with many vehicles. The rickshaw cannot be loaded with fish, meat, or vegetables, or other bulky items that may damage the rickshaw. If you want to turn, you must first extend your hand to make a sign to indicate the direction you are turning. When turning right, you cannot take a shortcut, you must make a large turn. Before stopping, you must raise your hand above your head to notify the vehicles behind. From night to dawn, you must light the rickshaw lamp. You cannot scramble for business, nor can you rush across the road to solicit business. If passengers leave items on the rickshaw, you must immediately send them to the nearest police station. When the car door cloth is not in use, it should be placed in the car compartment. The number painted on the car door cloth should be the same as the magnetic card number. After pulling a load, the soldiers should return the car to the car shop for washing.

Her two sons, Zhigang and Zhijiong, also ingested poison in succession. Fortunately, they were discovered early, and all three lives were saved and fully recovered at the hospital. However, the police considered Ms. Hu's actions too cruel and filed charges of abetment to suicide. Details of the trial were previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning was the scheduled date for the verdict. The defendant, Bao Hu, had previously been released to her husband, Bao Jianfu, after being reprimanded in court. She did not appear in court this time. Judge Liu Yugui of the First Special Court announced the verdict in the Eighth Tribunal, stating that Bao Hu was not guilty. The police's accusation of abetment to suicide was based on Bao Zhigang's written statement in the hospital. However, according to Bao Zhigang's testimony in court, his younger brother's ingestion of opium was not on his mother’s orders. Therefore, the charge of abetment to suicide could not be established.

Aborted Kidnapping of Qin Weiye: Five Kidnappers Convicted Yesterday; Three Were Involved in Crimes in the Chinese Concession: Municipal Public Security Bureau Requests Transfer for Investigation 125

Qin Weiye, managing director of the Tongyuan Bank on Tianjin Road, was about to go to work from his residence at the Lianzhuli alley entrance on Edinburgh Road on the morning of the 15th of last month. As soon as he boarded his car, kidnappers also got on the car, brandished a pistol, and threatened Qin and his driver, Wu Asheng, to remain silent and ordered them to drive off. Wu deliberately crashed into a passing trolleybus, causing the kidnappers to abandon their plan and flee. The Jing'an Temple police arrested several kidnappers, including Li Yizhi, and handed them over to the First Special District Court for investigation. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning was the scheduled date for the verdict. Investigating officers escorted the kidnappers to court at 9:00 AM. Judge Liu Yugui announced the verdict, sentencing Li Yizhi, Chen Yaonian, and Zhao Qinghong to 13 years of imprisonment each. Wang Shaoqing and Zhang Er were sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment each. All kidnappers were deprived of their civil rights for 10 years. After the verdict, Li Xiaobin, deputy captain of the Detective Team of the Ximen Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, arrived in court and stated that Li Yizhi, Wang Shaoqing, and Chen Yaonian were involved in major cases of murder and robbery in the Chinese Concession and requested permission to take them away for investigation. The court stated that the deputy captain did not have official documents, and they were ordered to wait for the Municipal Public Security Bureau's official documents before further review. Zhou Xinglou Accused of Joint Fraud: Interrogation Completed 126

Zhu Pingou, a staff member of the First Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, allegedly colluded with Zhou Xinglou, Peng Wu, and others, taking advantage of his position to defraud Ms. Qian Gu, a local woman, of 1,000 national currency units. After the victim found out and sought the return of her money, a balance of 830 yuan was still outstanding. Unable to recover the funds, a dispute arose. Zhu Pingou preemptively filed a lawsuit with the Procuratorate of the District Court, accusing Qian Gu of fraud and defamation. Prosecutor Xie Lian summoned the case for investigation and discovered that Zhu Pingou had committed fraud. He was prosecuted by law and indicted in the criminal court. As a result of the trial, Zhu Pingou was sentenced to six months of imprisonment and ordered to repay 830 silver dollars through a private lawsuit. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. It is now known that when Zhou Xinglou testified in court, he was biased toward Zhu Pingou. After careful verification of his testimony by Judge Lu of the Criminal Court, Zhou Xinglou was suspected of joint fraud. The case was transferred to the Procuratorate for investigation. After a clear investigation by Prosecutor Zhao Chuanjia, a public prosecution was filed by law. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Wu Xiangzu presided over the trial in the 13th Tribunal. Ms. Qian Gu and witness Jin Youxiang testified about the circumstances of the fraud. Zhou Xinglou, who was in custody, claimed that he introduced Peng Wu to Zhu Pingou, but knew nothing about the funds. The presiding judge considered the case clear and adjourned it. The verdict is scheduled to be announced at 2:00 PM on the 26th of this month. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Maritime Affairs Bureau Investigates in Detail: Xin Jiangtian Steamer Collision with Sailboat Case 127

The Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation received a report from the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company stating that the Xin Jiangtian steamer collided with a large sailboat while sailing from Ningbo to Shanghai, passing the Yawo Sand area. The sailboat was immediately destroyed and sank. More than ten people on board the sailboat were drowned and could not be rescued. No report has been received from the sailboat. The Bureau believes that the case is significant and has decided to conduct a detailed investigation. In addition to sending another letter to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, requesting a detailed report, it also sent a letter to the Customs Administration, requesting them to instruct the harbor master of the Jianghai Customs to send a report on the incident to the Bureau for investigation to determine the responsibility for the accident. According to news from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Xin Jiangtian steamer continues to operate on the Shanghai-Ningbo route as usual.

Tragic Murder in a Dance Hall: Deep Hatred Between Two Servants: Jin A'mei Kills Fan Maodi 129

The Lishu Dance Hall at No. 26 Zhubao Third Road in the French Concession was established by Fan Shoutang (47 years old, from Jiading, six miles from Liuhe Town) after the January 28th Incident. The business was quite good, and most of the patrons were Western sailors. Fan's family also lived there. Fan's cousin, Fan Maodi, 19 years old, had been working as a servant in the dance hall for four years. He was usually mature, hardworking, and was well liked by his employer, which led to friction with Jin A'mei, a colleague from Caojiadu in Huxi, who was in his forties. Maodi usually slept in a small room on the third floor, while Jin slept on a makeshift bed in the dance hall after closing. Recently, Jin’s resentment towards Maodi deepened, leading Jin to suddenly want to kill Maodi. After getting up at 9:00 AM yesterday, Jin A'mei hid a sharp knife and rushed into Maodi's bedroom on the third floor, bolting the door from the inside. He then used the sharp knife to stab Maodi in the chest near the right nipple, and then stabbed his right thigh, right calf, left hand, and left thumb, a total of eleven times. Maodi was awakened from his sleep by the extreme pain and cried out for help, but he was too weak to resist and could only await death. People nearby heard the cries but did not think it was a murder, so they ignored it and did not offer help. It was not until 9:30 AM, when the mistress, Fan Hongshi (Fan Shoutang's 36-year-old wife), got up, that someone told her that they had heard Maodi shouting for help and that he might be fighting with someone. Hongshi told her husband, Fan Shoutang, who rushed to the third floor to check. The door was bolted from the inside by Jin, so he kicked it open with force. Inside, he saw Maodi’s bed covered in blood. He was barely breathing and on the verge of death. The murderer, Jin A'mei, was sleeping on the bed opposite Maodi's after committing the crime. Seeing the employer enter the room, he became alarmed and stabbed himself in the right thigh several times with the knife. The owner, Fan Shoutang, called the people downstairs to come upstairs. First, they seized the knife from Jin's hand, and then they telephoned the Maitland Police Station to send detectives to investigate. They attempted to send the injured Fan Maodi to the hospital, but it was too late. He died. The body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall morgue for an autopsy. The murderer, Jin A'mei, was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. The detectives found the murder weapon on Jin's bed. It was reported that the knife was recently purchased. They also found the packaging paper and a suicide note stating his debts. The detectives took the shop owner, the chief steward Luo Baosheng, and the accounting clerk Xiao Zhou to the police station for interrogation. The body will be reported to the Second Special Court today for an autopsy. The deceased was said to be an only child. His mother died three years ago. His father, Fan Songyuan (50 years old), lives at No. 5 Rongqingfang, Jiu Mu Di, and is a foreign goods peddler.

Municipal Public Works Bureau徵工 to Dredge the Beixin Jing River Channel: Households Unable to Work Are Allowed to Pay a Substitute Labor Fee to Hire Labor 130

According to Datong News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau has prescribed measures for requisitioning labor for dredging the Beixin Jing River channel. For the benefit of households within the specified areas who cannot personally work, they are allowed to pay a substitute labor fee to hire labor. The announcement states: "Regarding the requisition of labor for the dredging of the Beixin Jing River channel in the Pusong District, all households within the designated 28th Bao Third Tu, West 19th Tu, 29th Bao First Tu, West Second Tu, Third Tu, Fourth Tu, Fifth Tu, Sixth Tu, and the designated 28th Bao East Second Tu, West Seventh Tu, who cannot personally work, are allowed to pay a substitute labor fee of 18 cents per cubic meter, to be used by the Beixin Jing River Dredging Office to hire labor. The payment method is that each household calculates the amount of earth to be dredged, and the substitute labor fee is submitted to the Tu Dong (area administrator), who will forward it to the Office. A receipt from the Bureau will be issued as proof. This announcement is made in addition to the public notice."

Coal Industry Association Telegraphed Ministry of Finance to Order Xiamen Customs to Use Domestic Coal for Ships 131

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Minister Kong [Xiangxi] of the Nanjing Ministry of Finance, esteemed Sir: According to a letter from the Xiamen Heping Company, the Customs has tendered bids for coal to be used by the inspection and engineering [巡工] ships under Xiamen Customs this year, and they intend to use foreign coal. The foreign coal receives a more favorable treatment by being exempted from import duties of more than four yuan. Our company feels deeply saddened upon hearing this. We know that your esteemed association speaks for the coal industry, promotes domestic coal, and spares no effort. Therefore, we report the facts in detail. Everyone knows that China's coal production is in surplus and that workers are unemployed. Both the government and the people have a duty to give priority to using domestic goods. Former Minister Song [Ziwen] set an example by limiting the use of foreign coal by Customs. The Customs should strive to uphold this principle and must not despise domestic coal, sit idly by while money flows abroad, and ignore the unemployment of workers. Furthermore, we found that there are also three or four domestic coal suppliers who bid for Xiamen Customs' coal besides foreign coal. The lowest price, including all domestic taxes, is no more than 18 yuan. Now, foreign coal is exempted from tariffs but still costs 17.2 yuan. If tariffs are added, the price is nearly 22 yuan. Why is the Customs not using inexpensive domestic coal and insists on using expensive foreign coal? Is it because foreign coal is unsuitable? Shanxi and Henan coal are comparable in quality to foreign coal. Both Xiamen and Shanghai Customs have used Shanxi coal for a year or two and have been satisfied. What is the reason for Xiamen Customs' sudden change of policy to purchase expensive foreign coal? We find it difficult to understand. Based on the above reasons, we do not know why the Inspection and Engineering Department made this decision. If it is to avoid tariffs of more than 4 yuan, then foreign coal is cheaper than domestic coal, so it must be purchased. If this speculation is correct, then all government agencies can follow suit, reducing national revenue and cutting off the livelihood of domestic coal. The impact will be enormous. Our company is concerned about the national economy and the people's livelihood and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we dare to send a letter to your esteemed association, asking you to uphold justice, forward it to party and government agencies, and ask them to prevent the use of foreign coal and select domestic coal for the benefit of the country.' Therefore, Customs is a tax revenue agency directly under the Ministry. If it abandons domestic coal and uses foreign coal, it violates the government's policy of promoting domestic coal. The impact on the national economy and the people's livelihood is enormous. We hereby telegraph, requesting your review and verification, and instructing Xiamen Customs to comply, select domestic coal to enrich the national economy. We await your reply. Shanghai Coal Industry Association respectfully presents."

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Organizes a Materials Purchasing Committee 133

Regarding the reorganization of the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, it is reported that the person in charge of the company's business department stated that the company has decided to organize a materials purchasing committee to handle the procurement of materials. The members of the committee will include the general manager, deputy general managers, department heads, the chief accountant, and one secretary. The general manager will serve as the chairman of the committee, and the two deputy general managers will serve as standing committee members. The committee has already started work and is drafting various regulations. It is expected that these measures will soon be implemented to ensure that the procurement of materials is rational and complies with economic principles. It is reported that the company's previous materials purchasing methods had many shortcomings. The most obvious is that the materials accounts within the company were not updated in a timely manner. In some cases, records had not been made for four months. At the same time, the quantity of materials recorded in the accounts was inconsistent with the actual quantity in stock. In such cases, the accounts are useless, and it is impossible to supervise the materials or check for irregularities. The company's material expenses, including fuel coal alone, reach about one million yuan per year, which is significant. Therefore, the establishment of the company's materials purchasing committee must, at a minimum, improve the materials bookkeeping system to achieve the goal of recording materials as they enter and exit, and to ensure that the accounts match the goods. It is reported that the purchasing committee has decided on the following purchasing principles: 1) Major materials: open bidding; 2) Temporary urgent and miscellaneous materials: open price inquiry and selective purchase. It is reported that General Manager Cai of the company is committed to making all aspects of the company's reorganization absolutely transparent, treating the company's problems step by step, and informing the public and employees of the root causes, so that they can contribute their opinions and cooperate sincerely to gradually realize the government's plan to reorganize the shipping industry.

Yude Lane Rent Reduction Dispute Resolved 135

The tenants of Yude Lane on Yunnan Road in the Public Concession demanded a rent reduction from the landlord, Lun Huan Company. After negotiations failed, they organized the Yude Lane Rent Reduction Committee and filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, which lasted for several months. Shao Ruqing sincerely mediated between the two parties. An agreement has been drafted and is held by Shao. According to the draft agreement, the rent for Yude Lane will be reduced to 80% from October 1, 1935, and 90% for shops along the road, for a period of two years. Shao announced the mediation process and the contents of the draft agreement, which was unanimously approved. As for the court case, the lawyers from both sides will reach a settlement in court when the next hearing is scheduled. The rent reduction dispute has now been completely resolved.
