Letter to the Editor 141

To the esteemed Shen Bao,

We, the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, extend our sincerest apologies for an error in yesterday's special edition commemorating the second anniversary of the New Life Movement in Shanghai. The article "Mayor Wu's Practice of the New Life Movement" was incorrectly arranged, with sections appearing in the wrong order due to a typesetting error. We are reprinting the original text below for correction.

Respectfully,

Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, February 19th

The New Life Movement, initiated by Chairman Chiang, has now been underway for two years. Deeply resonating with the needs of the era, it is rightly regarded as essential for national rejuvenation, fostering a positive trend and gaining widespread support throughout the country.

Looking back at China's recent history, various movements have sprung up successively. However, their impact has been limited, either to the advocacy of a few patriotic individuals, without being embraced by the general populace, or to momentary bursts of enthusiasm, lacking sustained momentum. The New Life Movement stands apart! It serves as the driving force for implementing new policies, revitalizing the nation, and advancing all cultural construction in China. The fundamental principles of the New Life Movement lie in the spirit of "if one day new, again new, daily new," and the resolve to treat "all things of the past as dead yesterday, and all things of the future as born today." Its aim is to sweep away all the entrenched vices and degenerate customs at the bottom of society, eradicate all the deeply rooted decadent habits in people's minds, and cultivate a new lifestyle of perseverance, integrity, and upward striving, so that the lives of people across the nation can become increasingly rational, scientific, productive, revolutionary, militarized, modernized, and artistic.

Life encompasses all human activities. It is the collective behavior of individuals and the nation to ensure survival, develop livelihoods, and propagate life. If the entire country, from officials to commoners, were rife with hypocrisy and corruption among officials, indifference and apathy among the people, decay and incompetence among adults, and depravity and indulgence among the youth, extravagance and superficiality among the wealthy, and baseness and chaos among the poor, then how could we hope to rectify national discipline, maintain social order, and achieve the liberation and revitalization of the entire nation? Therefore, transforming our lifestyle is not only crucial for reversing the tide of decadence and inspiring the people but also serves as the driving force for national rejuvenation, implementing new policies, and building all aspects of our culture.

Examining past movements for national salvation and reform, the reason they ultimately failed to achieve their goals lies in their impracticality and disregard for fundamentals. The implementation of any system is closely related to social customs and the habits of the people. China's past education and politics have been plagued by hypocrisy and a lack of practicality, resulting in ineffective laws, useless skills, and incompetent machinery. Even with identical official positions, efficiency varies; with identical skills, achievements differ; and with identical machinery, functionality is inconsistent. Therefore, after any nation undergoes reform and renewal, it must be influenced by customs and transformed by education for its governance to succeed. The effect of changing customs and habits is significantly greater, its application significantly broader, and its need significantly more urgent than that of political education. The New Life Movement is the central effort to change customs, inspire the people, and advance the nation's destiny. It is also the fundamental movement for national revival that cannot be delayed.

However, the success of this movement depends on the self-awareness and self-reliance of the people throughout the country. Only by setting an example can we extend it to others, spread it nationwide, create a prevailing trend, and form the strength of the era. Our nation has always been a land of propriety and righteousness, and the teachings of the ancient sages have long been admired by all nations. Yet, today, we still see the collapse of the four virtues (propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame) and the deterioration of discipline. Foreign countries even openly use terms like "unorganized" and "uncivilized" as a source of ridicule and scorn. This is not due to the ignorance of the Chinese people but to the empty words and arrogance of later generations who fail to practice what they preach.

Therefore, the essence of the New Life Movement lies in action, not empty words. The key to the success of the New Life Movement lies in the practice of propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame, not in various forms of propaganda.

Wang Yangming, a great Confucian scholar of his time, deeply understood the root causes of our people's problems and created the doctrine of the unity of knowledge and action. He said:

"The true and genuine understanding of knowledge is action; the clear and precise observation of action is knowledge."

"There is no knowledge without action; knowledge without action is merely not knowing."

"Sagehood is a single endeavor; knowledge and action cannot be separated into two things."

"Knowledge is the beginning of action, and action is the completion of knowledge!"

Yan Yuan (Xizhai) and Li Gong (Nugu), living at the end of the Ming Dynasty, also advocated the doctrine of action to stem the tide of chaos. Yan said:

"When a person studies, the thoughts in their mind and the words they speak, even if they have a thousand or a hundred meanings, are not as practical as putting one principle into practice."

"Better to be real in one end and one section than to be virtual in the whole body and great use."

"We should only put effort into practice, not into words and writing. Confucius's book is named 'Analects'; try to observe what the disciples recorded, and every sentence is about action."

"There is no other way to read books; just put effort into the word 'action.' For example, when reading 'he is filial and fraternal,' then strive to be filial and fraternal."

His disciple, Li Gong, continued his aspirations and also said:

"The classics are the register of virtue and skill, intended to promote practice, not to be read idly." Today, on the occasion of the second anniversary of the New Life Movement, I am honored to be asked by this association to contribute this humble piece. I am ashamed of my inadequacy and fear that this fundamental movement for national salvation and revival will repeat the mistakes of empty words of the past. Therefore, I offer these words in the hope of mutual encouragement. The success of the New Life Movement and the fate of the Chinese nation in the future depend solely on the actions of the Chinese people from now on!

The Paper Manufacturing Industry in Shanghai (Continued) (A Survey of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce, No. 14) 142

— Compiled by China Credit Information

3. Current Status of Paper Mills in Shanghai

Among the modern paper mills currently existing in Shanghai, the larger ones include Longzhang, Tianzhang, and about six or seven others. Their history and current status are described separately below for reference by all sectors:

1. Longzhang Machine Paper Company. Longzhang was established in the thirty-second year of Guangxu (1906) and is the third oldest paper mill in China. The factory is located at No. 5 Longhua Road, Shanghai, and the distribution office is at No. 17 Xinyongan Street. It is a joint-stock company. The current general manager is Mr. Pang Laichen, and the major shareholders are Messrs. Liu Baisen, Chuan Xiaoan, and Pang Zanchen. Pang Laichen is also a major shareholder. According to the company's previous registration with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, its capital was 343,000 taels of silver. The factory increased its capital once in 1933, but the exact amount is unknown. According to industry insiders, the total capital is about 1 million national currency. The company's factory buildings cover more than 20 mu of land and have two paper machines. Electricity is supplied by the factory itself. It employs more than 400 male and female workers. The factory focuses on manufacturing maobian paper and lian shi paper, using the double dragon as a trademark, specifically for printing and packaging by various stores. It is said that the monthly output is 300 to 400 pieces, and the annual turnover reaches about 1 million yuan. Two years ago, due to the Ministry of Finance increasing tariffs and the high price of foreign Daolin paper, Chinese factories had the opportunity to imitate it. The company ordered a Daolin paper machine from abroad, which was installed and put into operation in July last year. The Daolin paper of various weights produced is of excellent quality, comparable to imported products. It is sold through agents, with a price of 65 cents per pound. The factory's sales in other areas were previously mainly in North China, but now mainly in Central China.

2. Tianzhang Paper Mill. Tianzhang has two factories, East and West, which were formed by the merger of the former Lunzhang and Huazhang factories, as mentioned earlier. Lunzhang was originally founded by Mr. Li Hongzhang. In 1925, due to losses, it was merged into Tianzhang's West Factory. Before the merger, Yezhang had changed hands several times. In 1915, it was jointly operated by Chinese and Russian merchants, and later transferred to the Japanese Mitsubishi Corporation. In 1920, it was taken over by Liu Baisen and others and renamed Baoyuan Paper Mill. In 1925, it was renamed Tianzhang East Factory. Tianzhang initially had a capital of 400,000 taels of silver, which was later increased to 600,000 taels. When taels were abolished and replaced with yuan, it was increased to 800,000 national currency. The East Factory is located at Lujiazui in Pudong, and the West Factory is located at Huangpu Wharf in Yangshupu. The general distribution office is located at the intersection of Jiangxi Road and Sijing Road. It is a joint-stock company. Liu Baisen, Wang Xianhua, Liu Mengjing, Liu Zhongkai, Wang Xiaofen, and others are directors of the factory. It stopped production last year due to some events. After resuming production, it was renamed Tianzhang Changji. The East and West Factories both rent land to build factory buildings. The East Factory's base is more than 40 mu, with more than 60 factory buildings and warehouses. The factory has three wire paper machines, two Yangke paper machines, six beater machines, three digesters, one pulper, and one 500-horsepower steam engine, and five boilers. However, in 1933, a fire destroyed two machines. The factory purchased a calendering machine and a paper machine, equipped with an 85-horsepower motor, which was a German product and unique to the factories, worth about 120,000 yuan. The West Factory's base is about seven or eight mu, with one wire paper machine, two digesters, seven beater machines, and other paper machines and equipment, all of which are very complete. The two factories usually employ about 300 workers and more than 20 staff members. The factory's products include Daolin paper, imitation paper, No. 2 paper, husband paper, lian shi paper, and maobian paper, using the flying boat as a trademark. The East Factory produces coarse goods, such as yarn wrapping paper and secondary newspaper paper, with a daily output of 11,000 to 12,000 pounds to 15,000 to 16,000 pounds, and an annual output of 3.5 million to 3.6 million pounds. The West Factory originally manufactured Daolin paper, but later transformed to lian shi paper and maobian paper. Now it focuses on the manufacture of Daolin paper and imitation paper, which are widely sold. The daily output is 30,000 pounds, and the annual output is 7.5 million to 7.6 million pounds. The factory's products are mostly sold in Shanghai (major bookstores are its important customers), followed by Central and South China.

3. Jiangnan Paper Company. Jiangnan was founded in 1925, at a time when the boycott of Japanese goods was in full swing. The factory's Chinese paper, such as lian shi, maobian, and haiyue, had the opportunity to develop, but the output was not large. After the new machines were purchased, the anti-Japanese goods trend had passed. When the January 28th Incident broke out, the factory's products replaced Japanese goods and began to make huge profits (at that time, the daily shipments increased from 30 to 40 pieces to 200 pieces, which was still not enough to distribute). The main directors of the factory are Wu Yaoting, Yu Qiaqing, Sun Hongfen, and Zhang Jichen. The director and manager is Mr. Zheng Shouzhi. It is a limited company. The main factory is located at Guangfu Road, north of Caojiadu Creek, and the branch factory is located in Gaozi Zengkezhou (specializing in the production of reed pulp for the main factory). The office is located at No. 38 Avenue Edward VII. The factory's products use the Fortune and Prosperity (Fu Lu) as a trademark, and their quality is comparable to Japanese goods. The sales network covers the entire country. The factory's reed pulp, which is its raw material, is its patented invention. The Gaozi branch factory purchased 4,000 mu of land to cultivate and manufacture it, using the Three Rings as a trademark. The equipment of the main and branch factories is described below for reference:

Land base: The factory in Caojiadu, Shanghai, purchased a base of 18 mu, 4 fen, and 3 li. The Gaozi branch factory has a base of more than 100 mu, and also purchased more than 4,000 mu of reed land in Zengkezhou.

Buildings: In Shanghai, there is a three-story office building, a material warehouse, two selection rooms, one pressing room, one cooking room, one pulping room, two paper-making rooms, two cutting and finishing rooms, one packaging room, a product warehouse, a steam power room, all built with foreign pine and galvanized iron. In addition, there are water storage pools, a total water tower, a bleaching powder dissolution pool, a glue storage pool, an iron workshop, a woodworking shop, an electrical transformer room, an electrical switch room, a workers' dining room, a gatekeeper's room, and a 113-foot cement chimney. In the Gaozi branch factory, in addition to the boiler room, there are seven factory buildings, also made of foreign pine and galvanized iron, which are very strong.

Machines: The main paper-making machines in the factory now include one 100-inch round steel Yangke machine, two 65-inch round steel Yangke machines, two 12-inch diameter high-pressure digesters, eight Hollander beaters, two 30-foot long Lancashire boilers, sixteen German and French-made electric motors, totaling 400 horsepower, one large cooling machine with 150 horsepower (and one small machine, which is used for testing samples and is now used to manufacture coarse paper), and a large artesian well with a diameter of 12 and a half inches and a depth of 500 feet, equipped with a high-pressure air-cooled water pump, which produces more than 1 million gallons of water per day. There is also one 16-foot lathe, one 8-inch lathe, one 12-foot planer, and various tools such as drilling machines and pliers, three elevators, and 1,500 feet of small railway for loading and transporting goods. The Gaozi branch factory is equipped with one 28-foot long Lancashire boiler, one 5,000-watt electric light machine, one 48-horsepower steam engine, three 12-inch diameter high-pressure digesters, one towing machine, one rotary sawing machine, one four-roller calender, one shearing machine, one screening and cleaning machine, two belt conveyors, one bucket conveyor, two hydraulic reed pulp machines, and one hydraulic baling machine. The total value of the machines in the main and branch factories is very large.

In 1928, in order to develop, the company decided at the third shareholders' meeting to increase its capital in two phases: the first phase was to increase the capital by 600,000 yuan, combined with the original capital of 400,000 yuan, to form 1 million yuan. After the expansion, it planned to add a 65-inch paper machine to the Shanghai main factory to continue to imitate the production of domestic lian shi paper and maobian paper. It also planned to add three digesters and two pulping machines to the Gaozi branch factory to manufacture reed pulp, and to purchase 10,000 mu of reed land in Gaozi to produce more reeds! The second phase was to add 1 million yuan to form 2 million yuan, and to install two new paper machines and electrical equipment in the Gaozi branch factory to manufacture newspaper paper, glazed paper, Daolin paper, and wrapping paper. After the plan was proposed, many outsiders supported it. It is said that several hundred thousand yuan of the 600,000 yuan to be raised in the first step have already been raised. (To be continued)

Educational News

The Ministry of Education Revises the Table of Teaching Subjects and Class Hours for Elementary, Junior, and Senior High Schools 143

The Ministry of Education announced that the curriculum standards for junior and senior high schools have been in effect for more than three years. Recently, based on the opinions of the secondary education research associations of various provinces and cities and other parties, experts in various fields, and experienced middle school teachers and staff, a meeting was held at the Ministry of Education to discuss the revision of the middle school curriculum standards. As a result of the discussion, it was generally agreed that the teaching subjects and class hours should be slightly changed, and the content of the curriculum standards should also be revised. In addition, editing outlines for each subject should be added to make teaching more concrete. Based on this resolution, the Ministry of Education revised the table of teaching subjects and weekly class hours for each subject in each semester for junior and senior high schools and announced it on the 18th of this month for implementation.

Furthermore, the Ministry of Education promulgated the curriculum standards for kindergartens and elementary schools in October 1932, and schools across the country have implemented these curriculum standards for three years. Recently, based on the implementation status in various provinces and cities and the research results of the Elementary Education Research Association, the Ministry of Education convened multiple elementary education experts in October 1935 to hold a symposium on elementary school curriculum standards. The results of the association's research indicated that the elementary school curriculum still needed some revision. The total number of teaching hours at all levels was too high, and the burden on students was slightly too heavy, which has some impact on their physical health. The categories of subjects in the lower grades are quite numerous, making learning difficult to concentrate. In addition, there is a lot of repetition in one or two subjects, such as hygiene and nature, physical education and music. Based on the research results of the association, the Ministry of Education has held several meetings in recent times to discuss and decide to revise the entire curriculum. The main points of the revision of the elementary and middle school curriculum have been detailed in yesterday's newspaper. The revised table of teaching hours is recorded below:

Table of Teaching Subjects and Weekly Class Hours for Each Subject in Each Semester in Junior High Schools (Revised and Announced on the 18th of the Year 25 of the Republic of China)

Explanation

1. Physical education and Boy Scouts each account for two hours within the four hours. Boy Scouts have an additional hour of extracurricular training.

2. In the third year, depending on local conditions, labor, library, and music may be reduced by four hours, and vocational subjects may be added.

Table of Teaching Subjects and Weekly Class Hours for Each Subject in Each Semester in Senior High Schools (Revised and Announced on the 18th of the Year 25 of the Republic of China)

Explanation

Starting from the second year, credit hours are divided into Group A and Group B. Group A has six hours per week in both the second and third years (its level is equivalent to the content of the old standard's arithmetic curriculum). Group B has three hours per week in both the second and third years (its level should be reduced compared to Group A according to separately determined standards). However, Group B must add three hours of Chinese in the first semester of the second year, three hours of logic in the second semester, and three hours of English in the first and second semesters of the third year. The numbers in parentheses in the table indicate the hours for the subjects added by the two groups separately.

Schools may, depending on local conditions, set up simple vocational subjects (such as commerce, accounting, bookkeeping, statistics, application, clerical typing, arts, cooperatives, etc.) starting from the third year. Students who add subjects from Group A or Group B in the preceding paragraph may be exempt from the subjects added by the respective group in the third year.

Schools may set up domestic science subjects for female students. Female students who select subjects from Group B in the preceding paragraph may be exempt from the subjects added by Group B in the second or third year and select domestic science subjects for the same number of hours.

Library and music classes are taught in rotation every two weeks, one hour each time.

Summary Table of Elementary School Subjects and Weekly Teaching Hours (Revised and Announced on February 18, 1936)

Explanation

Civic training is different from other subjects and focuses on regular training. The table lists the group training time, which is 10 minutes per day (incorporated into morning meetings and other gatherings).

Social studies and nature in the lower and middle grades are combined into a general knowledge subject, including some knowledge of hygiene (hygiene habits are incorporated into civic training).

Starting from the fourth grade, the arithmetic subject adds teaching of abacus calculation.

Social studies in the upper grades can be divided into civics (civic knowledge), history, and geography. The time allocation is: civics: 30 minutes, history: 90 minutes, geography: 60 minutes.

Nature in the upper grades includes some knowledge of hygiene (habits are incorporated into civic training).

Fine arts and labor in the lower grades are combined into a work subject, and music and physical education are combined into a singing and games subject.

Total time: Schools may reduce 30 or 60 minutes per week depending on local conditions.

Time allocation: Based on the principle of 40 minutes per class, the duration may be extended to 45 or 60 minutes depending on the nature of the subject.

The Ministry of Education Issues a Circular Restricting Schools from Collecting Application Fees 144

Elementary schools and kindergartens are not allowed to collect fees.

Middle schools: half a yuan, vocational schools: one yuan.

(Nanjing, 19th) The Ministry of Education believes that schools in various places collect registration fees from new students without any restrictions, and many even misuse the funds without reporting them, making auditing difficult. In order to correct these abuses, it has formulated measures to restrict the collection of registration fees by schools at all levels and issued a circular to various departments on the 19th to instruct them to comply with the following key points: Elementary schools and kindergartens are not allowed to collect registration fees at all. The registration fee charged by middle schools should not exceed half a yuan in national currency, and the registration fee charged by vocational schools and above should not exceed one yuan. Registration fees should be used exclusively for the expenses of refreshments and meals for examinees. Advertising costs and test paper expenses should be paid from the school's office expenses during school holidays. Full-time teachers should not be paid separately for grading papers. Part-time teachers whose salaries are not calculated on a twelve-month basis may be given travel expenses at the discretion of the provincial and municipal education departments to ensure consistency. These expenses should be paid from the school's office expenses.

The strike was caused by students opposing make-up exams.

(Beiping, 19th) Tsinghua sophomores, in opposition to make-up exams, which the school refused to grant, surrounded the professors' office on the evening of the 19th, threatening a strike. The professors have also offered their resignations, creating a stalemate.

Yin Rugeng Appoints Principals of Tongzhou Model Schools for Boys and Girls 146

Ling and Wang, the new principals, issue a circular to teachers, staff, and students to return to school.

The male teachers are already in Beiping. The female teachers are also looking for a school site in Beiping.

(Special dispatch from Beiping) Education in Tongxian has been in a state of stagnation since Yin Rugeng's independence. According to sources from Tongzhou this morning (18th), the Jidong Autonomous Government recently formally announced Ling Ziping and Wang Ruishu as the principals of the Tongxian Normal Schools for Boys and Girls and issued a circular to the teachers, staff, and students of the former schools, urging them to return to school quickly. The reopening of the schools is scheduled for the end of this month, but most of the students of both schools are not in Tongxian and have already come to Beiping to find accommodation in order to resume classes. The situation of the two schools is recorded below:

The Hebei Provincial Tongxian Normal School for Boys, after the Jidong Incident, received an order from the Ministry of Education to suspend classes on the 12th of last year and move to Beiping. Now, after days of preparation, the school has found the old site of the Northeast Middle School in Pi Zi Hutong as its school building. Starting at 8:00 this morning (18th), classes officially resumed. The school has a total of nine classes, with 305 students. Except for more than ten students who have applied for a temporary postponement of registration due to the long distance, the remaining 280 students have returned to school from their hometowns to attend classes. According to Wan Shou, the principal of the school, who spoke to reporters this morning, in addition to the undergraduate students, the school also has an affiliated elementary school dedicated to students' practice. According to the regulations of the Ministry of Education, the number of students in the affiliated elementary school for normal school students to practice must account for a quarter of the total number. The affiliated elementary school has a total of ten classes in the junior and senior grades, with 450 students. Currently, some of the senior students have written to request the restoration of the affiliated elementary school, but the Department of Education intends to close the affiliated elementary school in order to save expenses. The school's previous monthly operating expenses were 6,200 yuan. The expenses for October since the incident have not yet been received, and only half of the expenses for December have been received. It is heard that the Department of Finance intends to issue half of the regular expenses in the future. However, this matter is being negotiated by the Director of the Department of Education, Li Jinzao, with the Department of Finance. The intention of the Department of Education is to strive to restore the original amount and restore the original classes to comfort the displaced students.

The Hebei Provincial Tongxian Normal School for Girls, since moving from Tongxian to Beiping with the Normal School for Boys, has not been able to resume classes due to the lack of a school building. Some of the students of the school are currently living in hotels and relatives' homes and have written to urge the school authorities to find a solution quickly.

Children's Educational Novel: Little Boy (1)(8)(1) 159

—Original by Louira Alontt, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Oh, Uncle John has been working at Mr. Lao's company all along. One of Mr. Lao's shareholders said that his concern for conscience in business was almost excessive, and he was beyond reproach in everything else. Another person said that money was not enough to repay Uncle John for his loyalty. Finally, what old daddy said showed his highest character. Once Uncle John was handling a matter at someone's place and later discovered that the person was trying to cheat and wanted Uncle to help him cheat. Uncle refused, even though the person offered him a high salary. He was not moved. The person was angry and said, 'If you stick to that principle, you will not succeed in business.' But Uncle retorted, 'Anyway, I never want to think about abandoning them to achieve success,' and left the job, preferring to take a harder and more difficult position."

"Good—Good!" Several students shouted in unison, because their mood at that time was most suitable for understanding and cherishing that story.

"He's not rich, is he?" Xie Ke asked.

"He's not rich."

"He never did anything earth-shattering, did he?"

"He didn't."

"He's just good?"

"But nothing else," Fu Lang answered honestly, secretly wishing that Uncle John had indeed done something to be proud of, because Xie Ke was clearly disappointed after hearing that answer.

Silk Industry in the Past Year 177

— Wang Tianyu

(1)

After the economic panic of 1929 spread throughout the world, people's purchasing power generally declined. This was followed by a sharp drop in prices and a decline in trade. Various production and consumption rates around the world also declined, with raw materials being the most affected. Silk is one of the raw materials, and it was naturally hit in the same way. However, because it is not a necessity, the rate of decline exceeded that of most raw materials. From 1929 to 1933, the silk trade rate fell by 74%, the silk fabric trade rate fell by 63%, the production rate fell by 11% from 1929 to 1934, and the consumption rate fell by 29%, resulting in the world's silk reserves increasing from 9.1 thousand tons in 1929 to 17.3 thousand tons in 1934. This was a new era in the history of the world, and Japan, the world's largest silk supplier, was busy limiting production in order to save silk prices and make up for the losses of domestic silkworm farmers. China is a country that lags behind in everything. Today, when the world silk market is entirely in the hands of the Japanese, the impact it receives is of course not just the economic panic. In addition to the dumping of Japanese silk and the surge in rayon giving it a major threat, it also suffers from the unparalleled pain of cheap gold and expensive silver due to the exchange rate between countries. According to customs reports, the silk export volume in 1934 was only more than 54,000 dan, and the lowest price of medium-grade factory silk in the Shanghai foreign market was 460 yuan per dan. As a result, only ten silk factories in Shanghai were open at the end of the year, with only about 2,000 silk reeling machines. Such an unprecedented order form has turned many lush mulberry forests in the country into cultivation areas for other crops. Although there has been government advocacy and management, and people's efforts to improve, it still feels deeply painful and difficult to achieve results in a short time.

(2)

In the first half of 1935, the silk market carried on the low-level trend of the previous year. Except for the first half of January, when overseas spring sales moved slightly and demand increased, the silk prices in the United States, Britain, France, and Japan rose in unison. Domestic silk factories also purchased a lot to replenish spring raw materials. At one time, silk prices were quite tight. In the Shanghai foreign market, the price of medium-grade factory silk once rose to 550 yuan per dan. However, the Chinese silk market continued to decline due to Japanese silk dumping, cheap gold and expensive silver, and relaxed exchange rates. After the US recovery movement was declared dead by the court in late May, it became even more depressed. By the end of June, the average price of medium-grade factory silk was only 420 yuan per dan, setting a new record that has not been seen recently. However, since July in the second half of the year, due to the slight economic recovery in the world, silk sales increased sharply. Furthermore, due to the reduction in silk production, inventories were scarce, which caused silk prices to gradually become firm. New York, London, Lyon, Yokohama and other ports all rose in unison. Among them, Lyon was inferior due to political unrest and other reasons in France, but the silk prices opened in other places in October have all exceeded the average monthly price in 1933. The Shanghai silk market also rose sharply. The price of high-grade factory silk once broke through the 1,000 yuan mark. Based on the data recorded in the Silk Statistics Monthly Report, the silk prices in the United States, Britain, France, Japan, and Shanghai, China in 1935 are recorded below:

Changes in the Silk Market in 1935

1933 Monthly Average 1934 Monthly Average 1935

Shen Bao National Products Special

Using National Products Movement 178

— Meng Zhao

In 1936, everyone shouted loudly! Shouting about the extraordinary period! But the strong also shouted about the extraordinary year! Their extraordinary is the extraordinary preparation period! Extraordinary period of aggression! And for the weak, it is just an extraordinary period of grievance, an extraordinary period of land loss, an extraordinary period of pain! To save decline! To deal with 1936, then only everyone should work hard to use the national products movement!

Using the national products movement! Or it may be a movement to save the country and survive! We must firmly adhere to the Three Noes Principles. In this life-and-death moment of the "Citizens Using National Products Year", the so-called Three Noes Principles are:

"Do not" use non-national products

"Do not" eat non-national products

"Do not" wear non-national products

If they are not national products, don't even look at them! Otherwise, they have the seductive power of a beauty! The legal currency in your own wallet will disappear without a trace. The author hopes that in this emergency, everyone will make sufficient efforts in the "Using National Products Movement"!

Contribution

Dispatching Warships to Nanyang and National Products Exhibition 179

— Yang An

The love of national products and the enthusiastic mood of Nanyang overseas Chinese are even greater than that of people in the country. However, they suffer from being separated by a vast ocean and do not know how the crafts of the motherland have progressed. They do not know what the quality and texture of the products are. Many overseas Chinese still measure the national products of the motherland with the eyes of twenty or thirty years. This is all because the overseas Chinese do not fully know the recent situation of national products. Therefore, there must be a large-scale national products exhibition in various parts of Nanyang, so that the general overseas Chinese can see and hear, and truly know the true national products in order to recognize the true national products. Recently, some Chinese people have seen this. Whenever there is an opportunity, they must transport national product samples to the exhibition. Recently, there has also been the organization of a Nanyang Business Inspection Group, so that domestic and foreign lovers of national products can unite and help each other. This is indeed a good work in the recent history of national products. However, the Nanyang region is vast. If it is fixed in one place, it will inevitably take a long time, lack sensitive functions, and will not be easily effective. I once talked with Mr. Xu, and Mr. Xu believes that China Merchants Steam Navigation Company should open a special ship to collect domestic products from the country, exhibit them on the ship, and invite local overseas Chinese to visit the ship in each place, and explain them and provide them with convenience. The visitors will feel like they have returned to their homeland and will be overjoyed. How great is its effectiveness? I have accumulated this idea for a long time, but I have not had the opportunity to practice this statement. Recently, the Shanghai National Products Movement Federation held a meeting, and someone suggested that the central government recently sent warships to Nanyang to comfort the overseas Chinese. Why not take this opportunity to collect products from various national product factories and hold a national product exhibition on the ship, so that the government can show the overseas Chinese the true face of the national products in addition to comforting them. Then the patriots will naturally think of admiring the motherland, and those who like to use national products will be happy to buy national products. I know that the government authorities have been recently encouraging national products and spare no effort, and social figures are particularly enthusiastic about foreign trade. They can work together to promote its success. According to the reporter's idea, the government authorities should be sponsored by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the Navy Department and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee should jointly prepare and designate a warship to set off on an appointed day: The collection of national product products can be assigned to the International Trade Bureau, the Commodity Inspection Bureau, the China National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association, and the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association to engage in product collection. Within three months, it can set off at the same time as the Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group. This is the most thorough method of promoting national products, and it is also the most glorious page in the history of national products. The reporter is happy and respects his eyes to see its success.

General Situation of Shanxi Industry 180

— Yi Yu

Shanxi is a relatively rich province in my country, and it is also the province with the most developed inland transportation in our country. Since the implementation of the provincial government's ten-year construction plan, various construction undertakings have had considerable success; especially for the revitalization of national products and industries, no effort has been spared. Up to the present, most of the daily necessities have been able to be self-sufficient, and there is little need to rely on other places. If we continue to work hard to promote it in the future, the achievements in the future will be truly unlimited. Therefore, if we want everyone to use national products, we must first revitalize our industry. This is a certain element. With excellent national industrial products, it is naturally easy to promote and prevail, and there is no need to seek foreign aid. We can know this fact by looking at the situation in Shanxi. However, although Shanxi's construction undertakings have made remarkable progress, the actual situation of its national products industry is not very clear to outsiders. Therefore, I will briefly describe the general situation of Shanxi's industrial progress to provide to readers.

Textile Industry Since the bankruptcy of the handicraft industry in Shanxi, social figures have realized that the demand is urgent, so they have launched textile industries that produce with new-style machines. However, due to the dumping of foreign goods and high costs, sales have been hindered and unable to develop. During the implementation of the provincial government's ten-year construction plan, thanks to the government's support, the declining textile industry gradually began to recover. According to recent statistics, there are a total of fourteen cotton textile factories in the province, with a total capital of approximately 800,000 yuan, and an annual output value of more than 11 million yuan, which is much more advanced than before. As for woolen textile factories, they are just beginning to sprout. There are only three in the province, with a total capital of 520,000 yuan and an annual output value of more than 50,000 yuan. The products of this kind of factory are quite popular among social figures, and there is a great trend of demand exceeding supply; therefore, its development should have considerable progress.

Machinery Industry The machinery industry is mostly expanded from the Ren Shen Manufacturing Plant, which was reorganized from the former arsenal. The capital is solid and abundant, and the products should be refined and civilian. At present, there are a total of five factories, with a total capital of 5,400,7,000 yuan (excluding one) and an annual output value of 598,000 yuan (excluding three). These factories are of great importance to Shanxi's construction work, so the authorities also pay special attention to them.

Chemical Industry The chemical industry is still in its infancy. The existing factories are listed below: Four match factories, with a total capital of 390,000 yuan and an annual output value of 300,000 yuan (excluding one). Three paper mills, with a total capital of 930,000 yuan and an annual output value of 300,9,000 yuan. One sulfur and saltpeter factory, details unknown. One glassware factory, with a capital of 10,000 yuan and an annual output value of 37,000 yuan. One leather factory, with a total capital of 200,000 yuan, details of the annual output unknown. One pottery factory, with a capital of 130,000 yuan, details of the annual output unknown. The only larger one in the building materials industry is the Northwest Cement Plant, with a total capital of 300,000 yuan, details of the annual output unknown. From this, we can know the immaturity of Shanxi's chemical industry. However, large-scale factories are always developed from the preliminary prototype organization, so they should not be ignored, and their development should be supported.

Other food and beverage industries, such as flour, tobacco, wine, and soda, the clothing industry, and the cultural industry are still lagging behind and have not made significant progress. But looking at the three items mentioned earlier, like the chemical industry, although it is not yet fully developed, it will definitely be able to develop smoothly in the near future. And the entire Shanxi's use of national products will also be realized.

A Visit to the Jiangnan Chemical Industrial Manufacturing Plant 181

— Hui

In recent years, China's chemical industry has been developing rapidly. The establishment of chemical industrial plants in this city is like bamboo shoots after a spring rain, showing a vigorous atmosphere. Taking the three acids that manufacture basic chemicals as an example, there is the Kaicheng Acid Manufacturing Plant that manufactures Sulphuric Acid, and the Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant that manufactures Hydrochloric Acid, both of which are very large in scale. Recently, the Jiangnan Chemical Industrial Manufacturing Plant was also established. I, as a reporter, was invited by Mr. Zhao Yechen, the manager of the plant, and Dr. Xue Jimin, the chief engineer, to visit the plant together with Mr. Pan Yangyao, Mr. Cheng Huanxi, and Mr. Shan Yanji. The following is a brief description of what I learned from the visit:

The Jiangnan Chemical Industrial Manufacturing Plant was established in April last year. Its main product is Glacial Acetic Acid, and its by-products are Wood Spirit or Wood Alcohol, Wood Charcoal, and Tar. The capital is set at 200,000 yuan in national currency, which was initiated and organized by Shen Shenyi, Zhang Rongchu, Zhao Yechen, Xue Jimin, and others. The address is at the intersection of Liuying Road on Gonghe Xin Road in Zhabei, with an estimated area of about 18 mu. The factory building is spacious and the layout is very reasonable. The arrangement of machinery and all engineering designs are planned by experts. In August last year, the production was successful, and the output and composition were able to meet the long-held wishes. The color of its glacial acetic acid reaches 99.5 degrees, and the wood spirit reaches 99 degrees, which is only seen in domestic industrial raw materials and can compete with imported products. What is especially rare and valuable is that the raw materials it uses are completely domestic products, such as the chestnut firewood from Huzhou, the sulfuric acid from the Wencheng Acid Manufacturing Plant, and the lime from the local kilns. These three are the raw materials for manufacturing products.

Currently, the factory has more than 80 workers. Its production capacity is 3,000 pounds of glacial acetic acid, 780 pounds of wood spirit, 130 dan of charcoal, and 6,000 pounds of tar per day. However, 3,000 pounds of glacial acetic acid is not enough to meet the needs of the market, so the factory can expand significantly.

The manufacturing process of the above-mentioned products is to first load the chestnut firewood onto iron cars, and then push the cars into the dry distillation pot via a light railway. Then, the pot cover is sealed and coal is burned under the stove. After about eight hours, the chestnut firewood in the pot evaporates due to heat, and part of it becomes gas, which rises through the flue. After passing through the tar filter, the oil sinks, and the remaining gas rises. A gas capture machine is used to pump the gas into a cooling pipe, where cold water circulates. The gas condenses when it encounters cold and becomes wood vinegar oil and sinks. (Note: This wood vinegar oil contains wood spirit, acetic acid and other impurities). Then it is sucked into a neutralization tank, and an appropriate amount of lime is added to neutralize it. It is mixed evenly with a mixer, and then introduced into the wood spirit tower, so that the wood spirit is separated. The remaining material is then passed through a steam engine dryer and a baking board to become dry Calcium Acetate (also known as calcium acetate). Then it is moved to the distillation section, combined with sulfuric acid, placed in a decomposer and steamed. At the same time, the mixer installed in the decomposer is turned on to continuously stir it, and the decomposition is accelerated by vacuum. After six hours, the lime contained in the acetic acid is absorbed by the sulfuric acid, and acetic acid of about 75 degrees is obtained and separated separately. It is then introduced into the crude acetic acid reactor and initially evaporated to remove moisture, which can be increased to more than 90 degrees. It is then steamed in a refined acetic acid reactor to purify it, and highly purified glacial acetic acid is obtained. As for the firewood in the dry distillation pot, it has been burned into charcoal. After a considerable period of time, it is dragged into the cooling pot, and after cooling, it is taken out and becomes charcoal.

As for the uses of the products, they are very extensive. Now, the use of each type will be described separately as follows:

Glacial Acetic Acid: It is a necessary raw material for the printing and dyeing industry and the manufacture of rayon. If glacial acetic acid is mixed with fuel, the fuel will never fade. In the past, the raw materials used by printing and dyeing factories in China were completely dependent on foreign goods. According to the import and export trade statistics of the customs, the total import in the past year reached 660,557 kilograms, valued at 311,343 yuan in national currency, of which goods from a certain country accounted for the largest proportion, accounting for about seven-tenths of the total.

Wood Spirit: It is a necessary raw material for celluloid factories, new medicine factories, and the manufacture of artificial emerald diamonds.

Charcoal: It is necessary for fuel, industrial and household use.

Tar: Also known as wood tar, it is mostly used for coatings for machinery and wood, and is a raw material for the rubber and paint industries.

After the visit, I feel that if China's chemical industry can strive to revitalize and increase production efficiency and reduce costs, there is hope to recover the tens of millions of leaks every year.

Random Notes on National Products 182

— Zhui Cheng

The newspaper reported: "Last year, from January to February, the total import of unnamed perfumes and cosmetics was 639,448 yuan." This is truly an alarming number!

Most of those who use cosmetics are rich people, and rich people often have the belief that "foreign goods are always better" imprinted in their minds. Therefore, the result is such a huge leak.

Cosmetics are not absolutely unusable, and domestic cosmetics are not necessarily all bad. For example, if he now uses "San San Perfume" and "Yi San Perfume" produced by the Wuzhou Factory, he will definitely not feel disappointed, and he can also reduce his expenses.

City merchants, inform all industries to promote domestic products with sincerity. "Promoting domestic products with sincerity" seems to be just empty talk, but in fact, to promote domestic products, the whole country must release "sincerity", otherwise, the future of domestic products will not develop no matter what.

Speaking of "dumping of foreign goods," isn't it because the Chinese people have no "integrity"? Therefore, on the one hand, they shout to promote domestic products, and on the other hand, the market is still full of imported goods. This is simply too insincere.

Therefore, to enable domestic products to defeat foreign goods, we can only hope that the people are full of "blood" and unite with "sincerity." This also depends on the efficacy of domestic tonics to generate blood.

Publishing Industry

Discussion on "Abridged Edition of Basic Classics of Sinology" 185

— Zhong Yi

In recent years, the reorganization of national heritage has occupied an important position in the publishing industry. No matter which bookstore is working hard to reprint ancient books. How good or bad this trend is, we will not ask for the time being; however, the many problems of being indiscriminate and mixed cannot be avoided.

The Commercial Press, which grasps the authority of the publishing industry, is also working hard in this area. The publication of the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries, the continuous publication of rare books, and the separate sale of the Series Integration and Basic Classics of Sinology can be regarded as its great contributions in these various aspects. The day before yesterday, there was another pre-order advertisement for the "Abridged Edition of Basic Classics of Sinology" in the newspaper.

In his green background, we can clearly see the reason why he wants to "abridge":

...The Basic Classics of Sinology are the bridge for those who study Sinology. Over the years, more than a hundred types have been published successively. The scope is widening day by day, and the total price is gradually increasing, and it is gradually felt that there is still a need for simplification. Therefore, choose fifty types of books from the series that everyone should read, which are "abridged"...

Indeed, the low price, selling one hundred and twenty books for only twenty yuan; convenient to carry, neat decoration, all use paperback six-open format; it must be regarded as the characteristic of this abridged edition. However, there must be some discussion about his simplification method and the fifty book titles obtained by the simplification.

This abridged edition is divided into twelve categories. They are reading guide, philosophy, social science, linguistics, applied art, fine arts, general collection of poetry and prose, separate collection of poetry and prose, ci and qu, criticism of poetry and prose, history, and geography travel notes. Among these twelve categories, the individual believes that there are many worthy of discussion, and now they are divided and discussed:

Reading Guide Category: This category selects four books: Book List Answers, General Theory of Classics, Pingyi of Various Philosophers, and General Meaning of Literature and History. According to personal speculation, the selector's intention must be that Book List Answers is a general theory, and the rest are divided into the four aspects of classics, history, philosophy, and collections. However, the individual believes that history and literature also occupy an important position in Sinology, and certainly cannot be included in one book of General Meaning of Literature and History. Therefore, the individual's opinion is that at least in the field of history, Zhao Yi's Notes on the Twenty-Two Histories should be added. (Because in terms of literature, there are two books in the category of poetry and prose criticism, which can be applied.

Applied Technology Category: The scope of the two characters of Sinology cannot be discussed here; however, the individual always believes that this category of applied technology does not seem to be included in this "abridged" narrow twelve categories. If applied technology can be successfully classified, then why can't medicine in the Inner Canon Suwen and Compendium of Materia Medica be successfully classified? Therefore, the individual's opinion is that the applied technology category should be cancelled.

Fine Arts Category: The two books already selected in this category can still be used, but the individual proposes to add two more. In the field of calligraphy, add Bao Shichen's Art Boat Double Oars; in the field of painting, add Zhang Yanyuan's Records of Famous Paintings of All Dynasties.

General Collection of Poetry and Prose Category: In this category, there are too many poems. There is only one book of essays, Selected Essays; the individual believes that at least one collection of essays that everyone must read, Ancient Prose Cizui, should be added, so that there will not be the problem of too few essays and too many poems.

Separate Collection of Poetry and Prose Category: There is a huge shortcoming in what is left out in this category, that is, writers before the Tang Dynasty were not selected. The individual believes that the collections of Tao Yuanming and Cao Zijian should be added to make it suitable. Otherwise, it is inevitable that there will be a biased form.

Ci and Qu Category: It is very strange that there is only a general collection of ci and no separate collection. It is also questionable to select Yangchun Baixue instead of Yuan Qu Xuan for the general collection of qu. Therefore, the individual's opinion is that separate collections of ci should be added by Bai Shi, Mengchuang, and Jiaxuan; and qu should be added by Yuan Qu Xuan.

History Category: The listing of four types of historical events from beginning to end is very good. However, it is also very strange to select Historical Records but not the other three histories - History of the Former Han, History of the Later Han, and Records of the Three Kingdoms. If it is said that the prose of Historical Records is good, then it should not be included in the history category at all? What's more, the prose of his three histories is not bad! Therefore, from the standpoint of history, the Four Histories must all be selected. The above is a discussion of all the categories it has. In addition to these seven points, the individual also has some opinions on other aspects, and incidentally put forward for discussion:

In the advertisement published by the Commercial Press, he said that this abridged edition has four major features. The first is "all important books are available." According to the seven points discussed above by the individual, it seems that this abridged edition is not up to this level. Can Essential Skills for the People's Welfare, Exploitation of the Works of Nature, and Tao Shuo (applied technology category) be considered "important books"? Can History of the Former Han, History of the Later Han, Records of the Three Kingdoms, Yuan Qu Xuan, and Ancient Prose Cizui not be considered "important books"? Therefore, these places are really a temporary rush for the Commercial Press and did not ask Sinology experts to choose, resulting in malpractices. We hope that the Commercial Press will not rush to publish and sell in the future. You must know that this has a great impact on the publishing industry and the future of culture.

Their third feature is that all sentences are punctuated. That's right, punctuating sentences can make reading easier and help understanding. However, Chinese ancient books often cause great disputes because of punctuation; therefore, punctuation is often a very important issue in Sinology. For example, scholars in the past had many questions about the punctuation of books such as Xunzi, Laozi, Zhuangzi, Mozi, Guanzi, Han Feizi, Shangshu, Zuozhuan, and Shiji. Therefore, the individual's opinion is that Chinese ancient books do not need to be punctuated, just let the readers understand it themselves. Otherwise, if there is a misjudgment, it will be a great harm.

The books listed in this abridged edition, some have annotations and some do not. The individual feels that it should be unified. Like the Han, Liu, Ouyang, and Wang collections in the separate collections of poetry and prose, there are Han Ji's annotations by Fang Shiju and Su Shi's annotations by Wang Xianqian, which can be used as references. It seems that readers do not need to print plain text like this.

In the minds of ordinary people in the past, novels were indeed considered insignificant: unexpectedly, there is no novel category in this abridged edition. The individual believes that the short stories of the Tang and Song dynasties and the Water Margin Dream of the Red Chamber of the Ming and Qing dynasties, at least, should be required reading for everyone; this cannot but be said to be a shortcoming in the selection.

I have said a lot above, and the individual is not attacking the Commercial Press. The individual is because it is an important and eye-catching member in the Chinese publishing industry, and I am afraid that I will dare to make extremely sincere contributions without considering my own taste.

Introduction to "History of Chinese Prostitution" 186

— Shou Qiu

The issue of prostitution is indeed a very important issue in social problems. Some people advocate public prostitution to prevent the spread of syphilis; some people advocate banning prostitution to stop the sin of adultery: we will not care about the right and wrong of these two arguments for the time being. But we can resolutely say that the cause of prostitution is the impact of social depression. Because the social economy is bankrupt, and women have no way to go, they have to resort to prostitution. Dr. Gu Hongming once said, "Prostitution of prostitutes is not prostitution, but selling poverty"! How painful this sentence is!

Regarding the opinions of Chinese and foreign scholars on prostitution, according to St. Thomas, "Prostitution of prostitutes in cities is like the sewers of palaces. If there are no sewers in palaces, palaces will become smelly." The German Berlier said: "Marriage is one side of the sexual life of the civilian world, and the other side is prostitution. Marriage is the positive side of sex, and prostitution is the inside." The famous German doctor Kuhn also said: "Prostitution is not something that should be tolerated, but it can be said to be a necessary evil. This, we will not care about it, and talk about the origin of the prostitution system. Some people think that it started with Guan Zhong. History tells us that Guan Zhong once set up three hundred women to facilitate travel. However, whether this prostitution was initiated by Guan Zhong is still necessary to study. It is a pity that there is no special book in China for reference. Although newspapers and magazines occasionally have records, they are all omitted and not detailed. This is really a pity!

Recently, the Life Bookstore has published a "History of Chinese Prostitutes", written by Wang Shunu. The price of the book is one yuan in legal currency, and the number of pages of the book reaches 356 pages. This book is a work of research on the prostitution system. The author narrates the origin of prostitution very thoroughly. The whole book is divided into six chapters: The first chapter is the introduction. The second chapter is the era of witch prostitution, from the Tang Dynasty of Yin Dynasty to the fall of King Zhou, which is the first period. It is counted from 1783 BC, a total of 644 years. The third chapter is the era of slave prostitutes and the occurrence of official prostitutes. From the Western Zhou Dynasty to the demise of the Eastern Han Dynasty, it is counted from 1122 BC to 218 AD, which is the second period, a total of 1340 years. The fourth chapter is the era of family prostitutes (ie, singing prostitutes) and slave prostitutes, from the Three Kingdoms to the demise of the Southern and Northern Dynasties and the Sui Dynasty (220 AD), a total of 435 years. The fifth chapter is the era of the most prosperous official prostitutes, namely the four dynasties of the Tang Dynasty; Song Dynasty; Yuan Dynasty; and Ming Dynasty (618 AD), which is the fourth period, a total of 1028 years. The sixth chapter is the era of private prostitution, since the Manchus entered the customs in 1644, which is the fifth period, a total of 288 years. The collection of various materials is very complete, and it can indeed be said to be a very valuable book now - when the prostitution issue has become an important social issue.

The material selection of this Chinese prostitution can indeed be said to be very extensive. At a time when the voice of banning prostitution is loudly sung, everyone can take a look at it; especially those who study the issue of prostitution should not miss it. Because this book not only describes the origin of prostitution and the evolution of prostitution, but also the causes of the prostitution system, the background of the prostitution system, the relationship between the prostitution system and society, we can all have a considerable understanding from this book, and we can also know a lot of interesting anecdotes about prostitutes. Therefore, I think this History of Chinese Prostitution needs to be introduced.

Finally, let me add a few words, that is, the author of the History of Chinese Prostitution, Mr. Wang Shunu, wrote this book entirely in the attitude of a scholar, for the study of people who study the issue of prostitution, and there is no personal opinion of the author in it, which is indeed commendable.

Bookstore Scenes (Continued) 187

— Li Hengzhi

(XI) Publishing New Books

Judging from the trend of publishing new books in new bookstores, except for one or two that have other specific policies, the entire new book industry is almost a history of speculation. Naturally, the publication of books by bookstores must adapt to objective needs within a considerable range, and sometimes they have to invent and then create the needs related to culture. However, if you just blindly follow the trend, follow others, and produce roughly, it is better to have no new bookstore than to have it.

If divided by the formal stage, the development of the new book industry can be said to have been caused by literary books. Under the heavy pressure of warlord politics, the best way for intellectuals to find relief is to seek expression in literature. Therefore, the romantic literature of creation in the early stage was very popular among young people, and the satirical writings of the Beiping Yusi Society were also admired by everyone. The establishment of the Creation Society's retail department, the relocation of the Beixin Bookstore, and the profitable business of Guanghua Taidong all caused a rush, and many new bookstores were produced. This trend can be called the literary period.

How to Watch Movies? (Below) 188

— Wu Mingyu

Third, this book indicates that movies are definitely not only simple "entertainment value". In addition to this function, it has a more important "social value". In other words, it is not only for people to pass the time occasionally, but also shows all aspects of life, analyzes the nature of things and problems, and provides people with good solutions and inferences. In fact, movies are not only a good thing for social entertainment, but also a useful tool for social education. Even if people who watch movies only seek entertainment, the audience's knowledge, attitudes, and behavior are unconsciously influenced by the consciousness of the screen.

Fourth, the book finally suggests that the production of future films should focus more on social and life issues, such as films similar to "All Quiet on the Western Front" and "The Outlaw" should be produced more. This is undoubtedly a very meaningful proposal. It also says: "The main purpose of future movies is not to make profits, but to educate and entertain the public." This is indeed accurate. Of course, whether it can be achieved in this way is another matter.

In short, this book is a good reading material for inspiring people to develop the ability to choose and appreciate movies. In addition to explaining the process and technology of film production, it also pays attention to the good and bad effects that movies can have on society, and proposes future reform plans. - The original work was compiled by experts designated by the American Educational Research Committee for young students to read. Mr. Hong Shen said in his preface: "I think there are three stages of movies. At first, it was just watching the excitement; a little more progress can watch the story; it must be that those who have a considerable understanding of film techniques can truly appreciate the art of movies. The basic knowledge mentioned in this book can indeed increase the reader's appreciation - and pleasure." I hope that Chinese movie audiences will all become appreciators in the third stage!

Finally, I have to say a word or two about the translation of this book. Although I don't want to do the work of proofreading or nitpicking, the writing style of the translation is not satisfactory. The sentences are often long and stiff, and one can tell at a glance that it is the result of "literal translation". Ordinary reading materials do not necessarily have to be "elegant", but they must not be "unreachable" because of seeking "faithfulness". The translator's writing style may be for the sake of "fidelity", but some places are too far from the conventions of Chinese literature, and even commas are used sparingly. For example: "Perhaps the most common error in using sound is the general attempt to accurately reproduce all the sounds found in real life." (page 177) "In superbly directed and cleverly constructed films, these various shots must be used so skillfully that you don't feel that you are applying a variety of camera distances." (page 139) This is just a random example. A good translation should make people - whether they know Western literature or not - read it very smoothly; unless the original work is dry and tasteless.

This book is listed as the tenth type of "Sunday Standard Book". Mr. Hong Shen selected it. According to Article 3 of the "Sunday Standard Book Publication Principles": "The writing style of the Sunday Standard Book must be clear and concise." This book has not yet reached this "standard". I think that although it is not necessary to re-translate, under the premise of not deviating from the original meaning, the translator should have the obligation to revise it in the re-edition, because the reason why "Standard Book" becomes "Standard Book" has objective value, and in today's need for film understanding, the general readers must not be discouraged or even lose courage because of this!
