Extra Edition of Shen Bao in This City

Casual Talk

Young Nun Rescued and Returns to Secular Life 203

— Zi Nan

Last autumn, Chen Wang, a woman from Chongming, brought her ten-year-old daughter Xiaomei to Shanghai to find her sister in Pudong. On the way, they were lured into the home of Bai Er, a rickshaw puller from the same village, who forcibly took her as his wife. Wang, unfamiliar with the area, had no choice but to submit. Later, Bai Er's father, Bai Dengtang, believed that Wang had mistreated his five-year-old grandson (Bai Er's son from a previous marriage), leading to his death. Bai Dengtang harbored resentment towards Wang. On the thirteenth day of the lunar new year, he secretly took Xiaomei away and, through the introduction of rickshaw puller Shi Guihua, sold her to Yongyuan, a disciple of the elderly nun Huilin, the abbess of Wanshou Convent in Shenjia Lane, Pudong, to become a young nun. The price was 30 yuan, and the broker fee was 2 yuan. After Chen Wang learned of what had happened, she was devastated and wept to everyone she met. Onlookers felt sorry for her and reported it to the police station in charge...who ordered all involved to be arrested and detained for investigation.

How will the aforementioned perpetrators be punished? This is a legal matter, and they are currently "arrested and detained for investigation," so we will leave it at that. Outside of the legal realm, we have two thoughts: First, the authorities are now in the process of registering maids, and yet such things still happen amidst the calls for maid rescue. This shows that the issue of rescuing maids is not simply a matter of rescue, but rather it will be included in the whole social problem, which can only be solved after the entire social system has been reformed; Second, the so-called monks and nuns, who should be free from worldly desires and have pure hearts, are no longer the original ascetics escaping from the world. Now, the so-called monks and nuns have been assimilated by capitalism and have become a "profession." The "Buddhist shops" that can be seen everywhere in Shanghai are undoubtedly the strongest evidence for this assertion.

How many people like Xiaomei in the "Young Nun Rescued and Returns to Secular Life" case, or similar to that, are there in the world? How many more future victims will there be? We cannot imagine it, and we dare not imagine it; however, one thing can be said for sure is that Xiaomei in the "Young Nun Rescued and Returns to Secular Life" case is just a small wave in the sea of similar victims.

Of course, what distinguishes Xiaomei from others is that, besides being sold, the buyer was a so-called monk who was supposed to be pure from worldly desires. Therefore, we have more feelings and a deeper understanding of this society. However, if we think further about this problem, for example, the current buyer was also bought by others in the past, then how would that be explained? Extending to the original instigator, why did they separate family members? Then, it would be difficult for us to give it an explanation based on personal gains and losses.

Separating family members should naturally be subject to the severe sanctions of the law, but sometimes legal sanctions seem insufficient, so what other measures should be taken? And whether the so-called registration of maids outside of the law can achieve the effect of preventing and prohibiting such things is what we cannot help but worry about.

On the Road 204

— Hei Ding

The mountain road was already dim. I stepped on the vast night, walking alone in the misty forest of Kakimoya Mountain. My heart was filled with the loneliness and solitude of the night. I was aimlessly searching for my wandering home.

Suddenly, two dark human shadows appeared in front of me, like two ghostly figures blocking my view. I heard a single, simple sound coming from ahead. I was so scared that I fell backward into the grassy thicket like a puppet. My head started to spin. My ears were buzzing. My eyes were filled with darkness. My heart was a turbulent sea. I shouted. However, a single, simple sound came from the front again, like thunder, flying far over my head.

I gasped for breath. I did not shout again. My throat was hoarse and parched. My face was covered in sweat. I stretched out my arms. I felt like those two dark figures were about to devour me. I didn't see their faces clearly. They were wearing dark, furry dog ​​skin hats on their heads. They were wearing dark, furry leather coats. They were making shooting gestures, each holding a small pistol: "Friend! We've been waiting for you for a long time..." My teeth were chattering. In a pleading tone, I said urgently:

"...Oh, oh...Friends, I, I, I am the same as you...Life has driven me into these mountains and fields...I have no money. I only have my restless soul, and the fighting muscles on my body...and, and, and the only small luggage roll that warms me. Moreover, there are two dry corn cakes wrapped in my small luggage roll. Friends, if you are hungry, I am willing to give them to you...If, if you don't believe my words are true, then, you can search me..."

I didn't say anything more. I faced them silently. Looking at their appearance, they seemed to be moved by my words. They looked at each other for a moment, one of them shook his head, looking sad, then quickly squatted in front of me and asked in a low voice, "Where are you going?"

"Nowhere definite..." I said miserably.

"Where did you come from?"

"Kuketobo..."

"Home?"

"Where is home! Home was destroyed in the fires of September 18th! I was driven out of my hometown by our enemies, and then I ran around everywhere..."

(The key to my memory was unlocked again: I seemed to have returned to my hellish hometown).

I was confused. I was sad.

The two "young robbers" in front of me (I actually called them that) were silent for a long time without saying a word. They stared at my face with melancholy eyes. (The night was black, and my face was black). Then, the one who was talking to me said, "Friend, then let's go find a place to stay together."

I didn't answer him immediately. I was timid and retreating: I was worried about my old coat, and I was even more worried about my only small luggage roll. Finally, I hesitated and murmured: "Well..."

He said straightforwardly: "What well... Don't doubt us..." After thinking for a while, he said again: "Once we meet, we are friends. If you think it is okay to be friends with us, in the future, we might as well live together. We are all young people..."

Before he could finish speaking, his companion stepped forward and patted me on the shoulder, interrupting:

"Two months ago, we never thought we would spend our wandering life in these mountains and fields. We were all young people who had received a university education. Since leaving school, we ran to the front line and participated in our anti-Japanese work along the Middle East line. Who knew that the war was unfavorable, and unfortunately our team was disarmed by the enemy. In this way, we all became prisoners of the enemy! After being imprisoned for two days, three of us were finally reborn. On the way to escape, within a few days, one of us died in a dilapidated small town on a late autumn night due to serious injuries. Since then, after losing a brave comrade, we also left that small town for the sake of life, and started running around in these mountains and fields. We walk every day. We also hide our bodies in the forests along the road every day. We use our alert ears to listen to the sounds on the road. Therefore, our hearts have gradually become sad. Our thoughts are like being covered by a black net. Regarding our lost actions, we deeply felt a sense of embarrassment and despair. Therefore, we often timidly stick our heads out of the forest and watch the backs of those who walk away. I remember once, we encountered a strong passing merchant, which made us feel confused! As a result, we were each hit hard on the legs by that guy, and he escaped..."

I couldn't help but ask anxiously: "Then why didn't you shoot him down?"

He smiled bitterly, then stammered, "Guns, hum... Since suffering from that guy, our legs have been aching for more than ten days, and we didn't dare to walk..."

In this way, we went on the road. I was no longer timid and retreating. The mountains and fields were as silent as a tomb. The night was quiet, the mountain road was quiet, as if our hearts were also quiet. Walking, walking, one of them, close to me on the right, gently patted my shoulder and said with a laugh, "Didn't you ask why we didn't shoot? Look, this thing can't knock anyone down!" As he said that, he took the gun out of his pocket and waved it for me to see.

I was surprised and took the pistol from his hand. I realized that his pistol was not a real one. It was a small toy that was very popular in toy stores and prepared for children: it could only make a sound but could not hit people. At this time, I couldn't help but laugh secretly in my heart: Ah, these are really two funny guys.

He grabbed my shoulder with his hand, humming a song, and said excitedly: "You, you, you, don't look down on this thing, you know, on this wandering and hungry road, it is our only savior..."

The moon rose high in the sky. A clear white light flowed in all directions.

I was not alone. I had two more friends.

Late at night, my friends and I stayed in the village of Nuoerzhake.

Pigeons 205

— Xinye

Occasionally, a pair of greyish-blue pigeons flew from the rooftop across from us, made a circle, and landed on the cement railing of the balcony. They looked around, leisurely beginning to pace back and forth, preening their wings.

I leaned against the window, gazing at those adorable shadows, vividly jumping and hopping before my eyes, and a scene from years ago floated up in my heart—In the past, I was not unfamiliar with these little creatures; when we were still in our hometown, three pigeon houses were kept in the old ancestral mansion—our old residence. Grandfather loved raising these things; he always played with the pigeons when he was free, and he often carefully changed their nests, added water, and cleaned their cages. During times of avian pox, he was even more diligent in stringing mung beans for them.

Page 20

Our banana residence had two rectangular small courtyards on either side. On the left was a tall Camellia japonica tree that reached the roof ridge, and on the right was a similarly planted magnolia tree. Inside was our bedroom. After we started keeping pigeons, two pairs of pigeon cages were placed in those two small courtyards, each cage having twenty-four compartments, but in reality, only sixteen pairs of pigeons lived there, with eight empty compartments. According to Grandfather, this was to prepare for any stray pigeons they might bring back to live with them.

Because among these pigeons, sometimes one or two pairs would fly away and not return, but after a few days, we would see them hurriedly flying back; moreover, some would even bring back one or two new companions. Therefore, Grandfather once told me:

"These intelligent little animals know how to love their home, but when their master's family declines, they will leave and never return. That's why there's an old saying, 'Ungrateful pigeons fly to prosperous places!'"

When we were young, those pigeons almost became our only companions in childhood. Hearing their cooing in the early morning or at dusk would make us feel joyful and very affectionate.

Standing on the nearby hillside, one could see the small red flag on the roof of our house fluttering in the wind from afar. This was said to be a marker to prevent the pigeons from getting lost when they flew out, unable to find their old home.

We were delighted by the arrival of spring when the geese came, because that was when we could fly pigeons with bells. Grandfather prepared many bamboo whistles in advance. In the morning sunlight, he tied the bamboo whistles one by one with red silk thread and fastened them between the pigeons' toes. When we now recall the impression in our memory at that time, we feel that Grandfather was not like an old man in his fifties, but rather almost as childlike as we were.

When the sky was high and clear, and the spring breeze was warm, we would often hear loud and melodious music in the sky in the mountains or deep valleys, which would evoke a sense of lightness and desolation in people!—This was the sound of the pigeons flying against the wind, causing the wind to enter the whistles.

After several years like this, Grandfather passed away in the autumn of one year; Father was also a wanderer living a nomadic life abroad, and the pigeons gradually went unmanaged. Although we loved the pigeons, I had already been sent to a private school to study, and I no longer had time to play with them. And as time passed, the shadows of those mischievous little things gradually disappeared from my heart.

About a year later, Father also passed away, so Mother, because she was so poor and had no other choice, sold those three pigeon houses—actually, only two were left at this time; one had escaped when Grandfather died—to my third uncle.

That story is almost twenty years in the past now, and for these twenty years, I have been wandering the crossroads of foreign lands. For the sake of life, for the sake of burdens, in those long days, I would never allow myself a moment of leisure to think about these distant past events, even though these stories still occupy a place in my memory, they only flash by occasionally and do not make the sadness of losing a childhood twenty years ago reappear.

Nonsense 206

— (Fool)

A fire broke out in the slums of Tianjin, killing over a hundred men and women. The cries shook the heavens; the scene was extremely tragic. Old Tan the Third is truly merciful and compassionate, saving as if rescuing from a disaster. This is a charitable undertaking that sustains life and provides for death.

In Gaoliu Village, Shuyang County, which is under the jurisdiction of Hai Prefecture, a "crying society" was discovered. On the Lantern Festival according to the lunar calendar, a large group of women gathered at the Earth Mother Temple in the village, linked arms, and wept bitterly. In red makeup and emerald sleeves, they lamented like swallows and warbled like orioles, incessantly throughout the night. Old Tan the Third says that the purpose of this crying society is still unclear to him. I cannot sympathize with this crying society, but in Chinese affairs, there is only crying; there is no other solution besides crying.

Interview 207

— Li Xuan

Jingzi looked at her father through the double wire mesh of the small window and felt that he didn't look like he did back home in the summer. His hair was long, his eyes were sunken and very large, and his whiskers surrounded his mouth in a furry way. Jingzi could see that her father was thin, as if he had been sick, but her father was smiling as he scratched his hanging hair and said:

"Jingzi, does (奶) miss Dad?"

Jingzi turned her bright little eyes, remembering that her (奶奶) had cried many times at home. Mom took Jingzi away from home, taking a rumbling train for two days. Last night, they passed through several brightly lit streets and settled in a courtyard full of strangers. When she went out in the morning, Mom had told her: "Don't tell Dad that (奶奶) often cries." At this time, she very sensibly twisted her small head of tousled hair, looked at Mom standing next to her, then looked at Dad's thin face, which was obscured by the wire mesh. Mom forced a smile and patted Jingzi's head, saying:

"Tell Dad."

In her little heart, she suddenly remembered that her (奶奶), with tearful eyes, often said that sentence:

"(奶奶) tells Dad to go home soon."

Dad smiled slightly, then quietly looked at Mom's face, which was pressed against the window frame. Mom didn't speak, her eyes slowly reddened, and she exhaled with a stuffy nose. After a while, tears fell in strings. Jingzi knew that Mom was sad, so she called out to Mom and cried quietly herself. Usually at home, when Dad came back from outside, he would hug Jingzi or kiss her rosy cheeks and ask:

"Is Jingzi naughty?"

She would definitely answer "No," or "Jingzi is a good child, not naughty." Dad would then take out candy from his pocket and stuff it into her chubby little hands, but now Dad seemed sick, locked in such a rat cage. A layer of gloomy shadow covered Jingzi's little heart, and she burst into tears, shouting

"Mom, let's go home with Dad!" (To be continued)

Little Monk: How did you get here?

Xiao Lu: We rowed our own small broken boat and drifted here with the wind!

Little Monk: Alright, come in with me!

Sound: Walking, the sound of the wooden fish gets closer and closer.

Little Monk: Wait here for a while, let me go in and take a look for you;

Lao Wu: Amitabha, this is really not easy!

Wang Damao: Finally there is salvation:

Xiao Lu: Let's take out our clothes and change them!

Lao Wu: Let's eat first, eating our fill is better than anything

A Qiao: That's right, why hasn't he come back yet?

(Walking, chanting Buddhist scriptures)

Storytelling with Stringed Instruments 210

Xu Wenbi's Opening Chapter

Shiyin (1340) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening Chapter "Understanding Romance"

One point of talent, one point of affection. Who is heartless, who is affectionate? Beautiful women all pity talented men. Talented men also love beautiful women. But there is one point that is regrettable. The length of affection is uneven. There are those who have affection on weekdays but can't meet. There are those who are unrelated but become intimate. There are those who begin with and abandon in the end. There are those who become Wu and Yue first and then get married. It's not that people's hearts are thick or thin. It's just that talent is shallow or deep. Is it the start of change today? There have been many people in the past. Admirable is Song Hong who didn't release a refined sugar woman. Lovable is Princess Lechang holding a mirror unmarried again. Detestable is Li Yi who is heartless and forgets old favors. Abominable is Wang Kui who intentionally goes back on his former oath. Dreaming of willows is all intimate. Writing poems on leaves also makes marriage. It's laughable how people are deluded. Stealing jade and fragrance is seen as proper. Deceitful couples recognize it as real. What's the point of fighting over jealousy? It only stirs up trouble and is not peaceful. Laughable - not understanding the two words of romance. Boasting of being talented men and beautiful women. Isn't it that they are misled by romance? The Yangtai is not a romantic pavilion. Even if romance is made, where is the truth? However. Being affectionate is not a matter of romance. Even if romance is light a little. I advise all romantic talented men. No talent, no affection. Making romance by force is the crime of romance. Enjoy love where you can get it.

Cheng Fangzhou, Li Pengsun, Mao Jiashu

Huamei (1060) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Romance of the Three Kingdoms - Changban Slope"

For thousands of years, heroes have talked about Zhao Zilong. Charging into the battlefield with a single spear. He is, wanting to find the young master, scolding Cao Ying. The snow-colored robe is stained with blood red. See him, tiger eyes staring in anger, spear piercing wildly. See him, wielding the treasure sword, his aura like a rainbow. Riding the horse and leaping into the encirclement. Fighting bravely is courageous. Scaring Cao Cao's heart to pieces. Asking to, what is his name, sending Cao Hong to find out. Loving talent and not bearing to harm him. Ordering the entire army, to capture him alive and capture him greatly. Who knew that wish was hard to fulfill. Cold arrows from the side dared not attack. Even with a body full of courage. The enemy soldiers are, thousands of troops trapped him. Searching for the ancient well and the crumbling wall. Seeing that, the main mother is in front of him, bowing. Kneeling to beg her to get on the horse. Madam Mi is, taking the chance to jump into the well's fence. Zilong is, busily hiding A Dou. Tucking close to the chest. Suddenly the enemy generals charge. Zilong is, drawing the spear and getting on the horse to battle the heroes. In an instant, the spear pierced, the sword slashed, and the heroes were killed. Had to, go to Changban Slope to find the lord. One horse galloping, dust covering the eyes. Hearing, the sound of drums knocking loudly. Suddenly seeing, Zhang Fei standing with a spear across, blocking the general, not letting go. Asking where he is staying.

Lu Qiuxia's Double Pearl Phoenix

Zhongxi (1040) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening Chapter "Jia Baoyu's Night Visit to Xiaoxiang Pavilion"

Severe winter frost freezes into ice. The moonlight is dim, about to break the soul. A gust of lake wind penetrates into the bones. The dark Grand View Garden is deserted. Baoyu is walking along the flower street. Night is silent, no sound is heard. He is a lamp. One person. Dark shadows rushing forward. Alone to Xiaoxiang Pavilion. To see if Lin's illness has lessened. Lightly knocking on the copper ring, dripping sound. Someone is quickly opening the door. Zijuan hears. Asking, is it Second Master wanting to enter. Quickly opening the door. Be careful of the cold of the deep night, not staying. Thank you sister for your concern. I am unforgettably grateful. Just because I can't stop worrying about you Lin. So, in the silent night, I have come. Walking to the sickbed. Seeing her gasping and weeping. Calling Lin at one moment. Calling cousin at another. Her almond eyes are open, not seeing clearly. Cousin, your second sister-in-law treats me too harshly. Her words are absurd, creating right and wrong. Although the old ancestor loves me. Sadly, I can't go to greet her. My past life's karma is cleared this life. Please don't look at this short-lived person anymore. Sister, you should throw away all your worries. Don't belittle yourself. I advise you to eat three meals a day. Add clothes to keep warm. I advise you to sleep early, not too late. Drink more medicine. I advise you not to listen to your sisters' words. They are like fake, like play, and like real. I advise you to protect your body and mind. Don't think of the old family in Yangzhou anymore. Hearing words. Tears trickling. Nemesis is most mindful for the slave. Cousin, please go back to the Yi Hong Courtyard early. Tears wet the silk scarf. This body may not be too adrift.

Movie News

"Wedding Night" Re-screening at the Carlton 212

— Bai Ling

A special production by Yi Hua Company, directed by Yue Feng, starring Yuan Meiyun, Wang Yin, Zhou Xuan, Guan Hongda, Jiang Xiu, Ye Wenqiu, Zhu Tianhong, Liu Li and other major stars, the full-sound dialogue blockbuster "Wedding Night," was previously publicly screened at the top-tier Carlton Theater in this city on Lunar New Year's Day. For a time, praise was universal, and it was widely recognized as an unprecedented masterpiece and supreme creation in the Chinese film scene. Therefore, although the initial four-day run was extended to nine days, the audience's enthusiasm only increased, showing a desire to continue indefinitely. However, due to contractual relationships, it was not possible to continue the run, leaving audience members who missed the screenings with regret. Since the end of the screening, Yi Hua and the Carlton have received dozens of letters and telegrams every day requesting a re-screening. In light of this, the two parties, after consultation, decided to re-screen the film with a brand new copy after "Song of Everlasting Regret" in order to reward the enthusiastic support of the audience.

Famous Film "Love Story of Singing Partners" 213

Screening at the Cathay Tonight

Lawrence Tibbett, the pillar of the New York Metropolitan Opera House, had not appeared on the silver screen for four years since co-starring with Loretta Young in "The Road to Glory." Due to the requests of fans everywhere and a generous offer from 20th Century Fox, he committed to filming "Metropolitan." To ensure the quality of the film, the company specially hired Boleslawski, the director of "Les Miserables," to direct the film. The film not only has a tragic love story, but Lawrence Tibbett also sings six of his best-known songs, including "Pagliacci," "The Road To Mandalay," "The Toreador Song From Carmen," "The Barber of Seville," "Faust," and "The Glory Road." The supporting actress is the beautiful star Virginia Bruce. The film is scheduled to be screened at the Cathay Grand Theater tonight (Thursday) at 9:15 PM.

News of the Stars 214

— A Luo

A Scene from "Peach and Plum Competing for Beauty"

The setting for "Peach and Plum Competing for Beauty" is a moonlit lakeside:

There is the quiet sound of flowing water, the graceful posture of willows, an endless expanse of grass in the distant fields, and the blue waves constantly kissing the pebbles on the shore, kissing the old roots of an old tree. The old tree is so thick that two people cannot embrace it, enough for you to lean on and ponder. Sparse branches, green leaves, everything is enough to evoke people's melancholy! This is not a place for frivolous men and wanton women to sing of love and dance, this is a place for a beautiful girl to secretly cherish spring, or for a lovelorn youth to vent .

Brief Account of "Old and New Shanghai"

"Old and New Shanghai" tells a story that takes place in a two-story building in Shanghai. An old landlord's eyes unfold the stories of various tenants, depicting the mysterious psychology of Shanghai people. There are dancers who earn a lot of money and are envied, couples who drive cars and are important people, and also unemployed poor wretches carrying heavy burdens. But the more important tenants are Wang Xianzai and Shu Xiuwen, a wonderful couple who win the aviation lottery and move from the front building to the garret to pretend to be poor! Hong Shen wrote the script, and Cheng Bugao directed.

"Spring Flower" to be Screened

Wu Cun's "Spring Flower" has completed the final scenes and is now in the process of editing. Once it passes censorship, it will be released.

In the sweet rhythm of the song "Spring Flower," Lao Gao's devotion encounters extreme pain, Yan Yuexian's stimulation leads to an unknown end, and Huang Naishuang is both loving the heartbroken man and rekindling his heart! Wu Cun hides a lot of tears behind these stories, saying that there can be no fire, no blood now,... The meaning, that kind of extremely painful meaning, is not difficult to guess. Pay attention to this noteworthy film.

Xu Wancheng's Compilation "National Survey of Universities and Schools"

Forthcoming Publication

Xu Wancheng, who graduated from Jiangsu Provincial No. 2 Normal School and Great China University and has taught for many years, is the chief editor of the "National Survey of Universities and Schools." The survey makes a systematic investigation of schools across the country, and the information of each school is investigated in detail. The education situation of each county and the addresses of primary schools are accurate. The work has been very intense recently. In addition to Yang Xiujun and others, Zhu Songyue, Zhu Longgu, Wu Zhiliang, and Zhou Wenhe have been hired to assist in the editing, and the book will be published soon.
